## FLAKY TEST (noticed+FIXED 2026-06-04): ktrace::self_test "Read back"
##   assertion `assert_eq!(last.category(), Category::General as u8)`
##   at kernel/src/ktrace.rs:458 occasionally failed on SMP when an
##   IRQ-category event from another CPU landed in the trace buffer
##   between the test's `record(General, ...)` and `read_recent`.
##   When it happened the panic showed left=5 (Irq) right=15 (General).
##   ROOT CAUSE: read_recent returns the newest events globally, not
##   per-CPU, so any remote-CPU IRQ recording wins the "most recent"
##   slot.  The test was authored when ktrace was UP-only / pre-SMP.
##   FIX: read_recent now requests a full BUFFER_SIZE window and the
##   test searches for the entry matching our unique magic tuple
##   (USER_EVENT + 0xDEAD + 0xBEEF) rather than asserting it's at the
##   tail.  Validated 3x in a row with no recurrence.

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): fork() self-test spawned a real ring-3 thread it never ran,
##   causing TWO distinct boot crashes (one after the other, as each was fixed). proc/fork.rs::
##   test_fork_clones_pcb originally used spawn_process to get a parent address space to clone.
##   spawn_process creates a *runnable* ring-3 thread (kernel stack + stack canary) that the test
##   never runs and tears down with pcb::destroy.
##   CRASH 1 (dangling thread → deterministic hang): pcb::destroy/destroy_process_resources frees
##   the address space (PML4 + mapped frames) but deliberately does NOT dequeue threads — its SAFETY
##   comment assumes the caller already killed them. So the never-run thread stayed Ready on the
##   scheduler run queue pointing at a freed address space. Boot ran cooperatively (no preemption)
##   through all later self-tests until apic::self_test() (main.rs:1124) enabled preemptive
##   scheduling ("[boot] Interrupts enabled — preemptive scheduling active") and spun; the first
##   timer tick dispatched the dangling thread → freed CR3 / IRETQ into a torn-down ring-3 address
##   space → triple-fault → QEMU halts (-no-reboot). Symptom: serial frozen at 1275 lines right after
##   "[apic] Running APIC timer self-test...", reproduced identically twice (deterministic, not the
##   flaky timing hangs elsewhere in this file). Note the fork self-test PASSED itself ~450 lines
##   earlier — the crash was the delayed consequence of its leaked thread.
##   CRASH 2 (canary false-positive, exposed once CRASH 1 was fixed by killing the thread):
##   see the dedicated stack-canary bug entry below. Killing the thread made it Dead, the
##   post-preemption reaper then checked its stack canary against the now-randomized per-boot canary
##   and FATAL-halted ("Stack canary corrupted for task 63 (fork-test-parent)! ... Found:
##   0xdeadbeefcafebabe") — 0xdeadbeefcafebabe is the FIXED fallback canary the task was planted with
##   because boot self-tests run before init_canary() randomizes it.
##   PROPER FIX (resolves both): the self-test no longer creates a scheduler thread at all. It builds
##   the parent address space directly — pcb::create allocates a PML4 (kernel half cloned), then
##   elf::load_segments maps the test binary's code segment — so there is no task, no kernel stack,
##   no canary, and no scheduler/run-queue/reaper involvement. This is also more faithful to the
##   construction-path intent (the test only ever needed an address space to clone). The REAL fork
##   path was never affected — fork_process destroys the child only BEFORE spawning its thread
##   (rollback) or AFTER a failed spawn (thread never ran), and build_fork_child spawns no thread.
##   LATENT-FOOTGUN note: pcb::destroy silently assuming no live threads is a sharp edge; any future
##   caller that destroys a process with live threads hits CRASH 1's class. Consider making destroy
##   defensively call kill_process_threads itself (idempotent). Not done now to keep the destroy
##   contract unchanged for the reap path; tracked here.

## BUG (noticed 2026-05-31, FIXED 2026-06-01, was latent/pre-existing, NOT fork-specific): stack-canary check
##   false-positives for any task created before the per-boot canary is randomized.
##   FIX APPLIED (option 1, the recommended one): Task now stores a `planted_canary: u64` field set at
##   creation in new_kernel() to the value actually written into the stack (snapshotted into a local so
##   the stack write and the field are guaranteed identical). new_idle/new_ap_idle set it to 0 (no
##   allocated stack, canary never checked). All three comparison sites now compare the read-back stack
##   value against the per-task planted_canary instead of the mutable global stack_canary():
##   Task::check_stack_canary() (sched/task.rs, used on context-switch-away and the dead-task reaper),
##   the canary_scan reaper diagnostic (sched/mod.rs ~2757), and the test_stack_canary self-test
##   (sched/mod.rs ~3818). This makes the canary stable for a task's whole lifetime regardless of when
##   the global is randomized, so re-randomization can no longer false-positive a pre-randomization
##   task. main.rs:2031 still reads the global stack_canary() but only to report "random vs fixed" in
##   the security banner — correct as-is. Boot test: "Stack canary: OK", StackCanary(random) active,
##   0 FATALs. (Option 2 — randomize before any task is created — remains blocked by CSPRNG init order;
##   option 1 is strictly more robust anyway.)
##   ORIGINAL ANALYSIS (kept for reference): The stack canary
##   is a single GLOBAL per-boot value (sched::task::stack_canary()), randomized via CSPRNG by
##   init_canary() at main.rs:714. But several boot self-tests create scheduler tasks much earlier
##   (sched self-test ~main.rs:439, thread self-test, proc spawn self-test main.rs:637) — i.e. BEFORE
##   randomization — so those tasks get the FIXED fallback canary 0xDEAD_BEEF_CAFE_BABE planted in
##   their stacks. check_stack_canary() (called on context-switch-away in sched/mod.rs:3534 and in
##   the deferred dead-task reaper at sched/mod.rs:2321) compares the planted value against the
##   CURRENT global canary. If such an early task is still around — specifically Dead-but-not-yet-
##   reaped — when the reaper runs after randomization, the values mismatch and the kernel FATAL-halts
##   as if the stack overflowed (it did not). Today this only bites a task killed-but-not-reaped
##   during the pre-randomization phase; the fork self-test triggered it (now fixed by not creating a
##   task). The other early self-test tasks happen to be reaped in-phase (before init_canary), so
##   they dodge it — but that's luck, not design. PROPER FIX options: (1) store the planted canary
##   per-Task at creation and compare against THAT, not the mutable global (most robust; makes the
##   canary value stable for a task's lifetime); or (2) randomize the canary before ANY task is
##   created — blocked today because init_canary needs the CSPRNG, which initializes after the early
##   self-tests; reordering boot so CSPRNG+canary come first would fix it generally. Recommend (1).
##   Zone: kernel-core (sched/task canary subsystem).

## BUG (noticed 2026-05-31, FIXED 2026-06-03, was pre-existing, NOT fork-related): gui/toolkit
##   (crate `guitk`) and every other userspace crate failed to compile under the default workspace
##   target (x86_64-unknown-none, bare-metal no_std). `cargo build` from the workspace root (which
##   is what scripts/boot-test.sh runs) built ALL members for x86_64-unknown-none and guitk emitted
##   2187 errors — e.g. "cannot find type `Vec` in this scope" (gui/toolkit/src/widget.rs:142 and
##   many more), plus E0405/E0408/E0425/E0433/E0463/E0531. guitk is a USERSPACE crate that needs
##   alloc/std and the x86_64-ouros target (its zone .cargo/config.toml), so it could not compile
##   for the bare-metal kernel triple. This broke the workspace-wide `cargo build` and therefore
##   the unmodified boot-test.sh.
##   FIX APPLIED (option 1, the recommended one): added `default-members` to the workspace
##   `[workspace]` table in Cargo.toml listing only the crates that build under the workspace-root
##   x86_64-unknown-none target — `kernel`, `posix`, `toolchain/stubs`. Userspace crates (apps/*,
##   gui/*, init/*, net/*, userspace/*) remain in `members` so they share target/ and so
##   `cargo build -p <crate>` continues to work from anywhere, but they no longer participate in
##   the default `cargo build` from root. Verified: `cargo build` from workspace root now finishes
##   cleanly (no -p needed). boot-test.sh's plain `cargo build` step now works as designed; the
##   `cargo build -p kernel` workaround is no longer required.
##   ORIGINAL ANALYSIS (kept for reference): guitk was added to default members or regressed
##   recently; investigation showed the workspace had no `default-members` filter at all, so every
##   crate in `members` was built by default. The proper fix was filter-based (default-members)
##   rather than excluding guitk from members entirely, because the latter would have broken
##   `cargo build -p guitk` and removed the crate from workspace target/ sharing.

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): CoW resolve over-decrement (mm/cow.rs resolve_cow_fault).
##   The shared-frame branch decremented the old frame's refcount once PER resolved 4 KiB PTE
##   (up to 4x for a full 16 KiB frame group) instead of once per address-space reference.
##   The per-frame refcount counts ADDRESS-SPACE references to the 16 KiB frame (set to 1 at
##   alloc_frame, +1 per fork, -1 per teardown which frees once per frame group via
##   step_by(HW_PAGES_PER_FRAME)), NOT per-PTE. So a write fault that broke CoW would drop the
##   count by up to 4 when it should drop by 1 — freeing a frame the forked child still maps
##   (use-after-free / cross-process data corruption) once fork() started sharing frames.
##   Latent until now because nothing called clone_address_space_cow yet; the existing
##   test_cow_resolve_shared self-test masked it by deliberately not asserting the post-resolve
##   refcount. FIX: decrement exactly once when pages_resolved > 0. Rewrote the comment block to
##   document the per-address-space convention (cites Linux do_wp_page/copy_page_range, which
##   also refcounts per struct page and adjusts once per broken shared mapping). Verified by the
##   new test_clone_address_space_cow self-test (refcounts go 1->2 on fork, child maps same phys).

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): POSIX getpid() used the WRONG syscall number.
##   posix/src/syscall.rs defined SYS_PROCESS_ID = 3, but the kernel
##   (kernel/src/syscall/number.rs) defines SYS_PROCESS_ID = 502 and has NO syscall numbered 3.
##   The posix file header explicitly says "must match kernel/src/syscall/number.rs". So
##   getpid() (posix/src/process.rs:159, syscall0(SYS_PROCESS_ID)) was issuing syscall 3, which
##   the kernel dispatch treats as unimplemented → returns NotSupported (-2): getpid() returned a
##   bogus/negative PID rather than the real one. An old posix `syscall_ranges_by_zone` test even
##   asserted SYS_PROCESS_ID <= 199 (kernel-core), encoding the stale assumption that process-id
##   was a low-numbered core syscall — but the kernel puts it in the kernel-process zone (500-599)
##   alongside SPAWN/EXEC/FORK. SYS_TASK_ID (2), SYS_PROCESS_SPAWN (500), SYS_PROCESS_PARENT_ID
##   (520) all already matched, so this was an isolated drift on SYS_PROCESS_ID. FIX: set posix
##   SYS_PROCESS_ID = 502, move its zone assertion from the 0-199 block to the 500-599 block, and
##   extend the new `process_syscall_numbers_match_kernel` test to pin EXIT/TASK_ID/PROCESS_ID/
##   FORK/SPAWN/EXEC/PARENT_ID to their kernel values. Verified: posix host tests pass.

## fork() LIMITATIONS (2026-05-31, documented, not yet implemented):
##   (a) HANDLE INHERITANCE is limited to refcount-capable same-id types: File, Pipe, EventFd,
##       StreamSocket (kernel/src/proc/fork.rs::dup_one). Channel, SharedMemory, CompletionPort,
##       and Timer handles are SKIPPED (child does not inherit them) because they lack a
##       refcounted same-id dup. A forked child that expected an inherited channel/shm/timer will
##       find it missing. FIX: add same-id refcounted dup to those subsystems (mirror pipe/eventfd),
##       then extend dup_one. Until then, programs needing those across fork must re-establish them
##       after fork (or use posix_spawn with an explicit handle map).
##   (b) END-TO-END RING-3 RESUME (the fork_child_trampoline IRETQ path) is NOT exercised by a
##       kernel self-test — only the construction path (CoW clone + refcount + PCB clone) is. A
##       wrong trampoline would triple-fault at boot, so validation is deferred to the POSIX
##       integration test / QEMU boot test. If fork misbehaves, suspect the [u64;17] register-image
##       offsets in fork.rs vs SyscallFrame field order in syscall/entry.rs.
##   (c) vfork() is implemented as plain fork() (no parent suspension / shared address space).
##       Correct but less efficient; documented in posix/src/process.rs::vfork.

## Judgment Calls (fork() implementation, 2026-05-31):
##   (a) SWAP-DURING-FORK: rather than add refcounting to swap slots, clone_user_half swaps any
##       swapped-out parent page back IN first (swap::swap_in_page with the fault handler's fixed
##       default flags PRESENT|WRITABLE|USER|NX) before CoW-sharing it. Simpler and avoids a
##       swap-slot refcount table. Reversible: if swap-slot refcounting is added later, fork can
##       share slots directly. Affects kernel/src/mm/cow.rs::clone_user_half.
##   (b) FILE-HANDLE INHERITANCE requires fs::handle refcounting. The child's userspace libc fd
##       table is CoW-copied, so it references the SAME kernel handle ids; the kernel cannot
##       rewrite that userspace table, so fork must bump refcounts on the existing ids (shared
##       open file description, same offset = correct POSIX fork semantics) rather than allocate
##       new ids. Pipes/sockets/eventfd already do same-id refcounted dup. fs::handle did NOT
##       refcount OpenFile (each id was a distinct entry, and handle::dup allocated a NEW id with
##       an independent cursor — that is dup()-of-fd semantics, not fork sharing). FIX in
##       progress: add refcount to OpenFile + fs::handle::dup_shared(id) (bump refcount, return
##       same id) + refcount-aware close. NOTE: the existing handle::dup independent-cursor
##       behaviour is ALSO wrong for the POSIX dup()/dup2() syscalls (which share the description);
##       that is a separate pre-existing bug, tracked here, not fixed in the fork change to keep
##       scope contained — fork uses the new dup_shared path.
##       >>> FIXED 2026-06-01: the POSIX dup()/dup2()/F_DUPFD bug is now resolved. The userspace
##       libc (posix crate) no longer calls SYS_FS_DUP for HandleKind::File in dup() (file.rs),
##       dup2() (file.rs), or F_DUPFD (fcntl_ops.rs::dup_fd_from). Instead File now shares the
##       source fd's kernel handle id at the fd-table level via alloc_fd_with_flags, exactly like
##       Pipe/Console/socket kinds. This gives correct POSIX semantics: dup'd file descriptors
##       share ONE open file description (shared offset + status flags). close() already gates the
##       kernel SYS_FS_CLOSE behind is_handle_referenced(), so the handle is released only when the
##       last referencing fd is closed. Kernel handle::dup (independent cursor) is UNCHANGED — it is
##       still used by spawn.rs fd inheritance and remains available for callers that genuinely need
##       a separate description. fdtable.rs module doc updated to reflect the shared-id model.

## Judgment Calls (wait-for-any-child / waitpid(-1) implementation, 2026-05-31):
##   (a) NO PROCESS GROUPS YET: POSIX waitpid distinguishes pid==0 (any child in the caller's
##       process group), pid<-1 (children in process group |pid|), and pid==-1 (any child).
##       We have no process-group subsystem, so the kernel treats ALL pid<=0 cases uniformly as
##       "wait for any child" (the pid==-1 semantics). This is correct for the common case
##       (shells/make use -1) and for any single-process-group workload. Reversible: when process
##       groups land, sys_process_wait's `pid_arg <= 0` branch should subdivide on the exact value.
##       Affects kernel/src/syscall/handlers.rs::sys_process_wait / sys_process_try_wait.
##   (b) SINGLE WAITER PER PROCESS for the any-child path: the any-child waiter TaskId is stored in
##       one slot on the PARENT pcb (Process::wait_any_task), unlike the specific-pid waiter which
##       lives on the CHILD pcb. If two threads of the same process both call waitpid(-1)
##       concurrently, the second set_wait_any_task clobbers the first's registration, so only one
##       thread reliably gets the child-exit wake (the other relies on its own try_reap_any at
##       block entry / a later wake). This matches typical single-threaded-waiter usage. PROPER fix
##       if multi-thread concurrent wait(-1) is needed: make wait_any_task a small list/set of
##       TaskIds and wake all of them. Tracked, not done (no current multi-waiter caller).
##       The clobber is at least SAFE — clear_wait_any_task only clears if the slot still holds the
##       caller's own TaskId, so a thread never clears another's registration.
##   (c) REAPED-PID via arg1 ABI: the any-child path returns the reaped child's pid to userspace by
##       writing an i32 to the arg1 pointer (posix waitpid passes a real &mut slot via syscall2),
##       while rax still carries the exit code (preserving the existing specific-pid ABI used by
##       init/services that call syscall1 with no arg1). The kernel writes arg1 ONLY in the
##       any-child branch precisely because syscall1 leaves rsi/arg1 holding a stale (possibly
##       valid, writable) pointer — writing it for specific-pid callers would corrupt their memory.
##       Affects handlers.rs::write_reaped_pid + posix/src/process.rs::waitpid.

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): userspace latent-bug sweep, batch 6 — stale DOCTESTS.
##   libservicebus's module-level doc examples didn't compile (2 failing doctests): they
##   imported a non-existent `EventHandler`, called `EventLoop::register` (real method is
##   `register_connection`), iterated `&events` where `wait()` already returns `&[Event]`
##   (so `&events` was `&&[Event]`, not an iterator), used `?` in a `fn main()` returning `()`,
##   and bound `conn` immutably though `send`/`recv` take `&mut self`. Rewrote both examples to
##   the real API, marked them `no_run` (they issue real IPC syscalls), and wrapped each in a
##   hidden `fn main() -> Result<(), libservicebus::BusError>` so `?` is valid. Verified the
##   doc + unit tests pass.

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): userspace latent-bug sweep, batch 5 — TEST HANG
##   (infinite block, not a failed assertion). Found because the full substantial-crate
##   `cargo test` run wedged on `vi`'s test binary ("running for over 60 seconds" for every
##   test, emitting `\e[999;999H\e[6n` to the captured output).
##   ROOT CAUSE (PRODUCTION bug, affects vi, htop, nano): their terminal-size detection has a
##   final fallback that writes the ANSI cursor-position-report handshake (move cursor to
##   bottom-right, send DSR `\e[6n`) and then BLOCKS reading the reply from stdin. Under a
##   pipe / file redirect / test harness (stdin is an open pipe with no data and no EOF) the
##   reply never arrives, so the blocking read hangs forever. vi calls this from Editor::new(),
##   which nearly every vi test constructs → whole test binary deadlocks.
##   FIX: guard the handshake behind `std::io::IsTerminal` — only perform the query when BOTH
##   stdin and stdout are real terminals; otherwise return the (24, 80) default immediately.
##   This also fixes the real interactive-use bug: piping into vi/htop/nano would have hung.
##   (Verified is_terminal() compiles+links on the x86_64-ouros target for all three.)
##   NOTE/follow-up: htop and nano parse the terminal reply with String::from_utf8_lossy,
##   which the coding standard forbids; low-risk here (reply is ASCII digits) but worth
##   replacing with a byte parse if these files are touched again.

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): userspace latent-bug sweep, batch 4 — RUNTIME test
##   failures (test builds compiled, but assertions failed) found by running the full
##   `cargo test --no-fail-fast` across all 275 substantial userspace crates. 10 crates.
##   PRODUCTION bugs (8):
##     - tcpdump (tcp_flags_string): flag emission order was arbitrary (SYN, ACK, FIN, RST,
##       PSH, URG), producing "[.F]" for FIN|ACK. Real tcpdump uses the fixed
##       `tcp_flag_values` order F,S,R,P,.(ACK),U. Reordered to match → FIN|ACK = "[F.]".
##       (Test for PSH|ACK expecting "[.P]" was a TEST-DATA bug; canonical is "[P.]" — fixed.)
##     - seq (regex_match_expr, group `\(...\)` capture): the inner subexpression only had to
##       match a PREFIX of the candidate slice, so `\(abc\)` against "abcdef" took the longest
##       slice (whole string) whose prefix matched → captured "abcdef". Fixed: inner match must
##       consume the ENTIRE candidate slice (consumed == sub_text.len()) for an anchored exact fit.
##     - login (verify_password): the locked-account guard lumped empty hash in with "!"/"*",
##       returning false and making the intended "empty hash = passwordless" block dead code.
##       Removed hash.is_empty() from the locked guard so an empty hash falls through to the
##       passwordless path (empty supplied password authenticates; non-empty does not).
##     - m4 (collect_args + Changequote): quote level was stripped in collect_args then
##       re-expanded by expand_args (double-strip). Fixed by re-wrapping the quoted text so a
##       single later expand pass strips exactly one level. changequote() with one empty arg
##       was mis-treated as "no args" (kept quoting on) instead of disabling quoting.
##     - du (human_readable/si_readable): whole-number special case printed "1K" where GNU
##       prints "1.0K". Removed special case; now <10 → one decimal, >=10 → zero decimals.
##     - crond2 (next_match_after): after zeroing seconds the computed time could fall BEFORE
##       `from` (same-minute truncation). Added a guard advancing to the next minute when so.
##     - dc (number scanner): hex digits A-F were not accepted as a number start nor inside the
##       number loop (used is_ascii_uppercase wrongly). Added 'A'..='F' to start arm and inner
##       loop; verified no command arm uses A-F.
##     - doas (tokenize): quoted strings were only recognised as whole standalone tokens, so an
##       embedded quote like PATH="/usr/bin:/bin" was kept verbatim. Unified into one token loop
##       that strips quotes appearing anywhere in a word, handles \ escapes, errors on unterminated
##       quotes, and uses a have_token flag so `""` still yields an (empty) token.
##   TEST-DATA bugs (2):
##     - date: epoch constants labelled 14:30:45 were actually 1_747_491_045 = 14:10:45 UTC
##       (20-min/1200s off). Corrected to 1_747_492_245.
##     - cpupower: test asserted format_freq_khz(1000) == "1000 MHz"; 1000 kHz = 1 MHz, fn was
##       correct → fixed the expectation to "1 MHz". (Also fixed a pre-existing collapsible_if
##       clippy deny in read_cpu_model via let-chain.)

##     - who: a real PRODUCTION copy-paste bug — the "who am i" detection was
##       `(a1=="am" && a2=="i") || (a1=="am" && a2=="i")` (equal_op deny; the second clause
##       duplicated the first). Replaced with the GNU rule (any two non-option operands →

##   it to the host x86_64-pc-windows-gnu test target broke linking with a flood of

##   (bcryptprimitives.dll / api-ms-win-core-synch). This meant `cargo test` on the

##   deny-by-default correctness lint (absurd_extreme_comparisons). At main.rs:1001
##   the keyboard-focus navigation tested `if col <= 0` where `col` is an unsigned
##   column index, so the `<` case can never occur — clippy flags it as always-equal-
##   to-`col == 0`. The intent is "tableau column 0 → focus Stock"; changed to

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): 17 apps failed `cargo clippy` (clippy::all/pedantic
##   deny breaks) — passwordgen, filesearch, snippets, dbviewer, undelete, renamer,
##   jsonviewer, qrcode, automator, sysmonitor, diagram, mediaconvert, photomanager,
##   slides, notes, email, torrent. ROOT CAUSE: each carried a per-file
##   `#![deny(clippy::all, clippy::pedantic)]` with an ad-hoc, incomplete allow-list and
##   did NOT inherit the workspace lint policy, so they tripped hundreds of pedantic/
##   restriction lints that the project DELIBERATELY relaxes in the root
##   [workspace.lints.clippy] (e.g. format_push_string is allowed precisely because its
##   clippy "fix" adds .unwrap(), which the project's unwrap_used lint discourages).
##   PROPER FIX (not a band-aid): made these crates adopt the centralized policy —
##   added `[lints] workspace = true` to each Cargo.toml and removed the divergent
##   per-file deny line (replaced with a short explanatory comment). This sets all=deny,
##   pedantic=warn with the documented allow-list, matching every other app.
##   That left only a handful of GENUINE clippy::all (deny) issues, fixed properly:
##     - filesearch/photomanager/notes: descending `sort_by(|a,b| b.x.cmp(&a.x))`
##       → `sort_by_key(|e| core::cmp::Reverse(e.x))` (unnecessary_sort_by).
##     - dbviewer: PartialOrd::partial_cmp delegated to a private cmp_value instead of
##       Ord::cmp (non_canonical_partial_cmp) → `Some(self.cmp(other))`.
##     - renamer: `loop { if let Some=.. {..} else {break} }` → `while let Some=.. {..}`.
##     - qrcode: factored a redundant boolean (nonminimal_bool) and replaced two
##       `for _ in 0..10 { v.push(false) }` quiet-zone loops with `extend(repeat_n)`.
##     - photomanager/notes: added `Default` impls delegating to `new()` (new_without_default).
##     - email: renamed inherent `ImapStatus::from_str` (returns Option, not the FromStr
##       Result contract) to `from_code` + updated its 3 test call sites (should_implement_trait).
##   All 17 now pass clippy clean; tests all green (1115 across the batch); ouros builds OK.
##
## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-06-01): 15 userspace tools carried the SAME divergent
##   per-file `#![deny(clippy::all, clippy::pedantic)]` + ad-hoc allow-list WITHOUT
##   workspace lints — ar, ftp, gdb, inetd, ldd, nmap, objdump, readelf, sftp,
##   ssh-keygen, sshd, telnet, whois, zip, stty. Same ROOT CAUSE as the 17-apps
##   entry above. These crates were only ever `build`-checked (cargo build does NOT
##   run clippy), so the per-file deny had been masking latent clippy::all errors.
##   PROPER FIX (same as the 17-apps precedent): added `[lints] workspace = true` to
##   each Cargo.toml and replaced the per-file deny+allow block with the standard
##   explanatory comment. nmap/whois also had a redundant per-file `#![warn(...)]`
##   for the defensive lints (unwrap_used/expect_used/panic/indexing_slicing/
##   arithmetic_side_effects) — removed because the root [workspace.lints.clippy]
##   already sets all five to warn. Preserved non-clippy `#![allow(dead_code)]`
##   where present (ar, gdb, objdump).
##   GENUINE clippy::all (deny) issues this exposed were then fixed properly — the
##   bulk via `clippy --fix` (with pedantic+defensive lints suppressed so only
##   clippy::all autofixes applied), and these remaining non-autofixable ones by hand:
##     - inetd: `loop {}` after the non-returning SYS_EXIT (empty_loop) →
##       `loop { core::hint::spin_loop(); }`; handle_tcp_echo `loop { match recv }`
##       (while_let_loop) → `while let Ok(n) = tcp_recv(..)`.
##     - ar: `uid/gid/mode: if opts.deterministic { 0 } else { 0 }` (if_same_then_else)
##       — both branches were identical because non-deterministic metadata
##       preservation was never implemented. Collapsed to the constants (uid=0,
##       gid=0, mode=0o100644) with a comment. SEE LIMITATION below.
##     - readelf: section-header ES column used `{:#02x}` (unused_format_specs — the
##       `#` "0x" prefix already exceeds width 2). GNU readelf prints entsize as a
##       plain 2-digit field under the 2-wide "ES" header → `{:02x}`.
##     - gdb: `find_register_index` for-loop (manual_find) → `(0..REG_COUNT).find(..)`;
##       C-ABI `main(argc, argv: *const *const u8)` derefs argv (not_unsafe_ptr_arg_deref)
##       — signature is fixed by the ABI so it can't be `unsafe fn`; added a justified
##       `#[allow(clippy::not_unsafe_ptr_arg_deref)]` (deref guarded by `argc > 0`).
##   nmap/objdump/sftp/zip had only autofixable clippy::all errors. All 15 now pass
##   clippy with warnings only (pedantic/defensive, per policy); ouros builds OK.
##   LIMITATION (ar non-deterministic metadata): OurOS `ar` always writes normalised
##   member metadata (uid=0, gid=0, mode=0o100644) regardless of the `-U`/
##   non-deterministic flag. GNU ar in non-deterministic mode preserves the file's
##   real uid/gid/mode. Not yet implemented — std on the ouros target (cfg unix)
##   exposes mode via MetadataExt, but uid/gid plumbing is pending. Low priority:
##   determinism is the common/default case and matters more for reproducible builds.
##

##   LIMITATION (systemctl systemd-escape modes): `systemd-escape --path` and the
##   default mode currently produce identical output. `escape_unit_name` already does
##   path-style escaping (strips the leading `/`, per test_escape_path), so the two
##   modes are not distinguished. Real systemd default mode keeps a leading `/` as a
##   leading `-` and does not strip trailing slashes; `--path` strips both. Low
##   priority (escape is a rarely-used helper); the `path_mode` flag is still parsed
##   and the discard at the use site is commented as intentional. To implement
##   properly: split into `escape_unit_name` (default, no leading-slash strip) and
##   `escape_unit_path` (strip leading+trailing), and route run_escape by path_mode —
##   but the existing escape_unit_name unit tests pin the path-style behaviour, so
##   that refactor must update those tests too.

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): apps/pinball — PRODUCTION combo-scoring bug. award_points
##   tracked the last scoring time in a u64 initialized to 0 and always took the "within
##   combo window" branch on the FIRST hit (since total_ms - 0 <= window), so the very
##   first hit was scored at x2 and the combo counter started at 2. Tests expect the
##   first hit at x1 (comment: "First: 100*1=100, Second: 100*2=200"). Changed
##   last_score_ms to Option<u64> (None = no prior scoring event) so the first hit, or
##   one after the window lapses, starts a fresh x1 combo and only consecutive in-window
##   hits increment. pinball 120/120 tests pass, clippy clean, ouros build OK.

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): apps/imageviewer — PRODUCTION navigation bug +
##   inefficiency. load_current_entry (called by next/prev/first/last_image and the
##   slideshow tick) delegated to open_file, which RE-SCANS and re-sorts the on-disk
##   directory and recomputes current_index by searching for the path every time.
##   So every navigation step did a full O(n log n) directory re-read, and if the
##   listing was set in memory (or the dir changed) the index reset to 0. Split out a
##   display_image(path) helper that only loads/shows the image; open_file calls it
##   then (re)builds the listing, while load_current_entry calls display_image alone.
##   imageviewer 94/94 tests pass, clippy clean (own code), ouros build OK.
##
## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): apps/filesearch — SEVERE PRODUCTION regex bug. The
##   regex engine's parse_regex_atom returned a bare `fn(u8) -> bool`, which cannot
##   capture a specific literal byte, so every literal character was matched as a
##   character CLASS instead: a lowercase letter matched `is_ascii_lowercase`, etc.
##   Consequently `world` matched ANY five lowercase letters — `^world` "matched"
##   "hello world" and `hello$` matched its tail. Character classes `[...]` were also
##   stubbed to "match anything". Replaced the fn-pointer with a Matcher enum that
##   carries Literal(u8) and a borrowed Class { body, negated }, added a real
##   class_matches (literals + a-z ranges + negation) and proper escaped-literal
##   handling (\\. etc. now match the literal char). filesearch 37/37 tests pass,
##   clippy clean (own code), ouros build OK.
##
## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): apps/calendar — PRODUCTION ICS round-trip bug.
##   ics_unescape used chained .replace() ("\\n"->newline, then "\\;", "\\,", "\\\\").
##   That mis-decodes an escaped backslash followed by a literal 'n' ("\\\\n"): the
##   first pass matches the trailing "\\n" as a newline escape, corrupting the value.
##   Rewrote ics_unescape as a single left-to-right pass that decodes each backslash
##   pair exactly once (\\\\, \\;, \\,, \\n/\\N per RFC 5545). calendar 52/52 tests
##   pass, clippy clean, ouros build OK.
##

##   production bugs. (1) test_mouse_click constructed a MouseEvent with a `modifiers`
##   field, but MouseEvent has no such field (E0560); removed it. (2) PRODUCTION:

##   test_minimax_prefers_win_over_block got a blocking move (0,2) instead of the
##   immediate winning move (1,2). Made minimax depth-aware (win = 10 - depth, loss =

## NOTE (2026-05-31): guitk::event::Modifiers gained a `super_key` field, which broke
##   the test builds of every app that constructed Modifiers with an explicit field
##   literal lacking super_key (typingtutor, stopwatch, metronome, game2048, pipes —
##   all fixed). Apps using `..Modifiers::default()` spread (crossword, mandelbrot,
##   maze, life, pong) or already listing super_key (freecell, solitaire, fontmanager,
##   wordle) were unaffected. Going forward, construct Modifiers via the NONE/ctrl()/
##   shift()/alt() builders rather than field literals so future field additions don't
##   break callers.

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): apps/regextester NFA engine — three correctness
##   bugs caused 8 matching/find/replace tests to fail. (1) execute_regex() seeded a
##   single thread at start_pos and never re-seeded, so it could not perform an
##   unanchored leftmost scan — \d+ on "abc123def" returned None because 'a' is not a
##   digit and the only thread died immediately. (2) A post-loop "final threads"
##   block unconditionally set end=input_len for any surviving Match thread, so
##   "hello" on "hello world" reported end=11 instead of 5. (3) The `*` and `?`
##   compilation set the Split's skip/exit branch to the Jump node (or the atom's
##   own body) instead of the node AFTER the loop: the inserted Split's targets were
##   computed in mixed pre/post-insert coordinates and adjust_after_insert() skips
##   the inserted node, so the exit index was off by one — "ab*c"/"ab?c" could never
##   match "ac". Rewrote execute_regex() as a proper Pike VM that seeds a new
##   start-thread at each position until a match is found (leftmost), tracks each
##   thread's true start, and prefers earliest-start/longest-extent; fixed the `*`
##   and `?` exit-index math (exit = post-insert index past the loop). Also corrected
##   test_match_digit, which asserted start==0 with the comment "NFA will start from
##   0" — that reflected the old start_pos-reporting quirk; the engine now reports
##   the true start (3) which is required for find_all/replacement to be correct.
##   Cleaned up pre-existing clippy errors in the crate (unnecessary_wraps,
##   needless let-match, items_after_statements, format-append→write!, unused_self
##   →associated fns, too_many_arguments allows). regextester 83/83 tests pass,
##   clippy clean, ouros build OK.
##
## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): apps/snippets — language auto-detection and the
##   tokenizer were wrong, plus clippy errors. detect_from_content() required
##   "fn " AND "let " AND "->" AND "::" all present to call something Rust, so most
##   real Rust snippets fell through to PlainText; relaxed to "fn " plus ANY of
##   let/->/:: . tokenize() returned zero lines for empty input (str::lines() yields
##   nothing for ""), so a freshly-created empty snippet rendered no line at all;
##   now pushes one empty line. Also fixed clippy errors (format-append→write!/
##   writeln!, unnecessary_sort_by→sort_by_key+Reverse). snippets 56/56 tests pass.

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): apps/startupmanager config deserialize() used

##   inside fields (escape_field escapes '|' as "\|"), so a description/path
##   containing '|' produced too many fields and InvalidField/MalformedEntry errors
##   on reload (caught by round-trip tests). Added split_escaped() which honours
##   backslash escaping when splitting, and switched deserialize() to slice

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): apps/weather format_temp() used "{:.0}" which
##   rounds half-to-even (banker's rounding), so 22.5°C displayed as "22°" instead of

##   (half-away-from-zero) before formatting. weather 112/112 tests pass.

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): apps/mindmap redo of node additions lost nodes.
##   MindMapApp::apply_forward(Action::AddNode) called MindMap::add_child(), which
##   allocates a FRESH node id. After undo/undo then redo/redo, the first redo
##   re-created node A under a new id, so the second redo (re-adding child B whose
##   stored parent_id still pointed at A's ORIGINAL id) found no such parent and
##   silently dropped B (node_count stuck at 2 instead of 3 — caught by
##   test_multiple_undo_redo). Added MindMap::add_child_with_id() which restores a
##   node under its original id (and shape) and refuses if the parent is missing
##   or the id is taken; apply_forward now uses it so parent references survive
##   redo. mindmap 118/118 tests pass.

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): apps/diskimager HashState::finalize() produced
##   colliding digests for short inputs. update() distributes input bytes across 8
##   state words by idx%8, but finalize() emitted the raw words then truncated to
##   the digest length, discarding words 4-7 for SHA-256 (and 2-3 for MD5). Two
##   short inputs differing only in a byte that mapped to a discarded word (e.g.
##   "data A" vs "data B" — differ at index 5 → word 5) yielded identical digests
##   (caught by test_hash_different_data_different_hash). Rewrote finalize() to
##   fold the ENTIRE internal state plus bytes_processed into every output word
##   (rotate/xor/multiply mix), so each input byte influences the final digest
##   regardless of slot. NOTE: HashState is still a non-cryptographic placeholder
##   ("would use a proper crypto implementation" per its own comment) — it must be
##   replaced with real MD5/SHA-1/SHA-256 before image verification is trusted.
##   diskimager 112/112 tests pass. (Also: nearby FAT dir-name handling at
##   main.rs:584 uses String::from_utf8_lossy — violates the bytes-not-UTF8 rule;
##   left as-is for now since it's display-only, but should become OsStr/bytes.)
##
## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): apps/videoplayer PlaybackSpeed::label() emitted
##   "2.00xx" instead of "2x". It formatted with format!("{:.2}x", v) — embedding
##   the "x" suffix BEFORE trimming trailing zeros — so trim_end_matches('0'/'.')
##   found no trailing zeros (string ended in 'x'), then a second "x" was appended.
##   Fixed by formatting the number alone ("{:.2}"), trimming, then appending "x".
##   videoplayer 93/93 tests pass.
##
## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): gui/toolkit Color::over() integer overflow.
##   color.rs alpha-compositing computed `channel as u16 * da * inv_sa` which
##   peaks at 255*255*255 ≈ 16.6M and overflowed u16 → debug panic (caught by
##   paint's test_pixel_buffer_blend). Rewrote with u32 intermediates and a
##   precomputed destination-alpha contribution (da*inv_sa/255); numerators now
##   peak at ~130k, well within u32. guitk 598/598 + paint 155/155 tests pass.

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): vi search wrap-around landed on the cursor's
##   own position instead of the next/previous match. userspace/vi/:
##   test_search_fwd_wraps failed. Both search_fwd and search_bwd had the same
##   off-by-one: the loop computed r = (row +/- i +/- 1) so at i==0 it visited
##   the NEXT/PREVIOUS line, yet applied the cursor-column skip (col+1 / col-1)
##   to that wrong line; the starting line was then revisited LAST with
##   start_col=0 / before=len, re-matching the cursor's own position. E.g.
##   forward search for "abc" from row2,col0 of ["abc","def","abc"] returned
##   row2 instead of wrapping to row0. Rewrote both to visit nr+1 (line,col)
##   pairs starting at the current line (skipping the cursor) and ending with
##   the current line again, rejecting the cursor position on the final wrap.
##   Fixed search_bwd too (same root cause; no test covered the multiline wrap).
##   53/53 tests pass; cleaned 5 clippy warnings (incl. while_let_loop).
##   Clippy-clean host + ouros; builds for ouros.

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): apps/installer test harnesses hit the UAC
##   os-error-740 launch failure ("installer" contains "install"). Unlike the
##   single-binary crates, installer has BOTH a [lib] and a [[bin]], so cargo
##   test builds TWO unit-test harnesses (installer-<hash>.exe each). The usual
##   embed_manifest() fix only emits `rustc-link-arg-bins`, which covers the bin
##   + bin unit-test but NOT the lib unit-test. Fixed by ALSO emitting the broad
##   `cargo:rustc-link-arg` scope (applies to the lib unit-test build) pointing
##   at the same OUT_DIR/embed-manifest.o object. (`rustc-link-arg-tests` is
##   rejected as an invalid instruction by this cargo / no [[test]] target.) The
##   broad scope also re-covers bins so the object links twice there, which is
##   benign — harnesses launch without UAC (proving a valid asInvoker manifest)
##   and it only affects host test artifacts; the shipped OurOS binary embeds no
##   manifest. 86/86 lib tests pass; 9 clippy warnings cleaned (lib + grub.rs).
##   Clippy-clean host + ouros; builds for ouros.

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): patch mis-applied normal-diff append.
##   userspace/patch/: test_end_to_end_normal_add failed — "1a2" (append after
##   line 1) produced ["b","a","c"] instead of ["a","b","c"]. apply_hunk always
##   computed target_start = old_start + offset - 1, but a pure insertion
##   (old_count == 0) names in old_start the line to insert *after*, so the
##   0-indexed insertion point is old_start (no -1). The -1 is only correct for
##   delete/change where old_start is the first affected line. Fixed by
##   special-casing old_count == 0. 61/61 tests pass; 7 clippy warnings cleaned

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): install had 2 failing tests AND the same

##       embed-manifest (build-dependency). Harness then launched: 27 passed,
##       2 failed.
##     * REAL PRODUCTION BUG in parse_symbolic_mode: setuid/setgid/sticky bits
##       were silently masked out. The code OR'd the special bits into perm_bits
##       (s -> 0o6000, t -> 0o1000) then computed `effective = perm_bits &
##       who_mask`, so e.g. "u+s" gave 0o6000 & 0o700 = 0 and "+t" gave
##       0o1000 & 0o777 = 0 — both special bits vanished. Fixed by tracking
##       has_setid/has_sticky separately: apply setuid (0o4000) when who
##       includes owner or no who specified, setgid (0o2000) when who includes
##       group or no who specified, sticky (0o1000) always. 29/29 tests pass.

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): apparmor had 4 failing tests (two real

##   userspace/apparmor/src/main.rs:
##     * PRODUCTION BUG 1 (#include swallowed as comment): parse_rule_line()
##       checked `trimmed.starts_with('#')` (return) BEFORE the include check,
##       so AppArmor's classic `#include <abstractions/base>` directives — which
##       start with '#' — were treated as comments and never recorded. The
##       `#include` branch was effectively dead code. Reordered: handle include
##       directives before the comment guard. Fixes test_parse_rule_line_include,
##       test_parse_profile_with_includes, test_full_profile_parse_and_validate.
##     * PRODUCTION BUG 2 (variable use misread as assignment): preprocess_

##       (`@{var}=value`) and `continue`d without expanding. So a rule line that
##       merely USES a variable at its start (`@{HOME}/data r,`) skipped
##       expansion entirely. Fixed: only treat as an assignment when the closing
##       brace is followed by `=`; otherwise fall through to expansion. Fixes
##       test_preprocess_variable_expansion. 139/139 tests pass.

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): avahi had 1 failing test (off-by-one in
##   the autoipd conflict limit) + ~10 pre-existing clippy errors.
##   userspace/avahi/src/main.rs:
##     * test_autoipd_max_conflicts failed: AutoIpd::step in the Conflict state
##       gave up one retry too early (`_conflict_count >= MAX_CONFLICTS`).  The
##       test does MAX_CONFLICTS (10) conflict/retry cycles and expects each to
##       succeed, then a final conflict to be fatal.  Changed the check to
##       `> MAX_CONFLICTS` so exactly MAX_CONFLICTS retries are tolerated and
##       the next conflict is fatal — see JUDGMENT CALL below.  192/192 pass.
##     * ~10 pre-existing clippy errors: write! ending in "\n" -> writeln!,
##       collapsible if/match (auto-fixed 9); Ipv6Addr::new's 8-arg signature
##       (too_many_arguments) #[allow]'d with a comment since it mirrors
##       std::net::Ipv6Addr::new and the segment count is inherent to IPv6.
##   Clippy-clean host + ouros; builds for ouros.
##
## JUDGMENT CALL (2026-05-31, avahi autoipd MAX_CONFLICTS semantics):
##   The conflict counter previously failed when count >= MAX_CONFLICTS (10),
##   i.e. it tolerated only 9 retries.  The unit test encodes the opposite
##   intent (10 retries tolerated, fail on the 11th conflict), which matches
##   RFC 3927 §2.2.1's "exceeds MAX_CONFLICTS" wording.  I changed production to
##   `> MAX_CONFLICTS` to align with the test + RFC rather than relaxing the
##   test.  Easy to reverse (one comparison at AutoIpd::step, Conflict arm) if
##   the human prefers the stricter "give up at the 10th conflict" reading.
##

##       are implemented + unit-tested but unreachable from the CLI entry points.
##       Reserved with #[allow(dead_code)]; wiring them into the dispatch path is
##       a deferred improvement.

##       `-A POSTROUTING -j MASQUERADE` carry no `-t`, so the parsed Command
##       defaulted to the `filter` table and `execute_command` applied nat rules
##       to filter -> "chain 'POSTROUTING' not found in table 'filter'".  Added
##       Command::table_mut() and override the parsed command's table with the

## BUG (noticed+FIXED 2026-05-31): tr range expansion was completely broken.
##   userspace/tr/src/main.rs expand_set() guarded the `a-z` range branch with
##   `&& i > 0_usize.wrapping_sub(1)`, i.e. `i > usize::MAX`, which is ALWAYS
##   false — so the range branch was unreachable and `tr a-z A-Z` (the single
##   most common invocation) treated `a-z`/`A-Z` as the three literal bytes
##   'a','-','z'.  4 unit tests (test_expand_range/digit_range/upper_range/

##   and the redundant nested conditions; a dash is a range separator iff a

## BUG (noticed 2026-05-30): SYSTEMIC — a swathe of userspace tools call
##                            WRONG syscall numbers because they hand-roll
##                            raw `syscall` wrappers instead of using std.
##
##  SEVERITY: high (functional + safety).  Several user-facing tools do not
##  work at all, and some invoke privileged/unintended syscalls.
##
##  *** CORRECTION (2026-05-30): the original premise below — "std::time is
##  broken, std issues raw Linux syscalls that hit the wrong native handler"
##  — is WRONG.  std actually WORKS on this OS.  The userspace target links
##  against the sysroot's libc.a + libstubs.a (toolchain/sysroot/lib), and
##  the `posix` crate implements the libc symbols (clock_gettime, open,
##  read, write, rename, statvfs, mkfifo, utimensat, ...) as `extern "C"`
##  functions that route to NATIVE OurOS syscalls.  So std::time calls the
##  posix `clock_gettime`, which calls syscall0(SYS_CLOCK_REALTIME=14) /
##  syscall0(SYS_CLOCK_MONOTONIC=10) — the correct native numbers — and
##  std::fs / std::net / std::process likewise route through posix.  This is
##  confirmed: nmap and stat now use std::fs/std::io/std::time/std::process
##  and build clean for x86_64-ouros.
##
##  THEREFORE the proper fix for any hand-rolled tool is simply to USE STD
##  (std::time / std::fs / std::process), not to hand-correct raw syscall
##  numbers.  The earlier per-tool number fixes (date/at/dig/rsync/scp/etc.)
##  are functionally correct but are the wrong *approach*; they should be
##  migrated to std in the broader audit below.  For the handful of POSIX
##  ops std doesn't expose (statvfs, mkfifo, utimensat) declare a thin
##  `extern "C"` binding to the posix symbol — see stat for the pattern.
##
##  ORIGINAL (now-disproven) ROOT-CAUSE ANALYSIS, kept for context:
##   1. [DISPROVEN] It was believed std (os=linux/musl) issued the *Linux*
##      clock_gettime syscall (rax=228) directly via the SYSCALL instruction,
##      and that since kernel rax=228 = SYS_PIPE_POLL, std::time returned
##      garbage.  In fact std calls the libc `clock_gettime` *symbol*, which
##      our posix crate provides and routes to the native no-arg clock
##      syscalls.  std::time works.
##   2. Independently, each hand-rolled time tool wrote a raw `syscall`
##      wrapper — with NO shared source of truth for the numbers, so they
##      each guessed differently and mostly WRONG:
##        - at, date, nmap:           SYS_CLOCK_GETTIME = 40  -> kernel 40 = SYS_PORT_READ
##        - date:                     SYS_CLOCK_SETTIME = 41  -> kernel 41 = SYS_PORT_WRITE
##        - dig, rsync, scp, screen,
##          tcpdump:                  SYS_CLOCK_MONOTONIC=30  -> kernel 30 = SYS_IRQ_REGISTER
##        - stat:                     SYS_CLOCK_GETTIME = 228 -> kernel 228 = SYS_PIPE_POLL
##        - inetd, sshd:              SYS_CLOCK_MONOTONIC=10  -> CORRECT (kernel 10)
##      They also assume a POSIX combined ABI clock_gettime(clock_id,
##      timespec*) that the kernel does NOT provide.
##
##  KERNEL CLOCK ABI (the authoritative, correct interface — number.rs):
##    SYS_CLOCK_MONOTONIC = 10  no args; returns boot-relative ns in rax (i64)
##    SYS_CLOCK_REALTIME  = 14  no args; returns wall-clock ns-since-epoch in rax
##    SYS_CLOCK_SETTIME   = 15  arg0 = target_epoch_ns (u64); 0 / -EINVAL
##    SYS_CLOCK_ADJTIME   = 16  arg0 = signed delta ns (i64 bit-pattern); 0 / -EINVAL
##  There is NO combined clock_gettime(clock_id, *ts) syscall; each clock is
##  its own no-arg syscall returning a single ns value in rax.
##
##  CONSEQUENCES OBSERVED (by reading the code; not boot-tested):
##    * date: reads time via SYS_PORT_READ(=40) and `date --set` writes via
##      SYS_PORT_WRITE(=41) — i.e. completely non-functional, and the set
##      path aims a port-I/O syscall at hardware (gated by the port-I/O cap,
##      so likely EPERM rather than real harm, but it is the wrong syscall).
##    * ntpd & hwclock: read/set the clock via /proc/time, which has NO
##      provider in procfs (no "time" arm in generate()) AND procfs is
##      read-only (no write_file).  So both cannot read or set the clock;
##      ntpd's read falls back to unwrap_or(0) => treats time as 1970, and
##      its writes are silently discarded (`let _ = write_system_time(...)`).
##    * ntpd additionally truncates all corrections to whole seconds
##      (offset_us / 1_000_000), so even with a working setter, every
##      sub-second NTP correction (the normal case) becomes a no-op.
##    * dig/rsync/scp/screen/tcpdump: their "elapsed time" calls hit
##      SYS_IRQ_REGISTER(=30) instead of clock_monotonic.
##
##  RELATED KERNEL GAP (separate, also document/fix): sys_clock_settime and
##  sys_clock_adjtime (handlers.rs ~3941/3966) do NOT check CAP_SYS_TIME —
##  the capability gate lives only in the userspace posix wrapper
##  (security_settime64).  A process issuing the raw syscall sets/steps the
##  wall clock with no privilege check.  The cap check belongs in the kernel
##  handler (defense in depth); userspace gating is advisory only.
##
##  PROPER FIX (architectural — pick one; recommend B short-term + A later):
##   A. Implement the Linux syscall-translation layer (roadmap 5079) so
##      os=linux std "just works" and the Linux numbers map to native
##      handlers.  Large; fixes std + all Linux-numbered callers at once.
##   B. Provide a shared `oursys` (or extend an existing shared userspace
##      lib) crate with audited NATIVE clock wrappers (realtime/monotonic
##      no-arg ns reads; settime/adjtime), and migrate every time tool to
##      it.  Removes the per-tool hardcoded-number duplication that caused
##      this.  Reversible; correct regardless of whether A lands later.
##   Also: add CAP_SYS_TIME enforcement inside sys_clock_settime /
##   sys_clock_adjtime.
##
##  STATUS (2026-05-30): documented here in full and migrated the raw-syscall
##  callers to the native ABI (all build clean for x86_64-ouros):
##    * date  — realtime read 40->14 (no-arg ns), set 41->15 (single-ns);
##              dropped the bogus clock_gettime(clock_id,*ts) form + dead
##              Timespec.
##    * at    — realtime read 40->14 (no-arg ns); dead Timespec removed.
##    * nmap  — RTT timer 40->SYS_CLOCK_MONOTONIC=10 (monotonic is the right
##              clock for elapsed-time measurement).
##    * stat  (FULLY FIXED 2026-05-30) — this multi-personality binary
##              (stat/touch/ln/readlink/realpath/mkfifo) hand-rolled ELEVEN
##              filesystem syscalls with wrong Linux numbers that collide with
##              unrelated native syscalls (SYS_STAT=18 unassigned, SYS_LSTAT=19
##              unassigned, SYS_FSTATAT=20=SYS_MMAP, SYS_UNLINK=10=
##              SYS_CLOCK_MONOTONIC, SYS_RENAME=41=SYS_PORT_WRITE, SYS_STATFS=42=
##              SYS_DMA_ALLOC, SYS_UTIMENSAT=35, SYS_LINK=37, SYS_SYMLINK=38,
##              SYS_READLINK=39, SYS_MKFIFO=40=SYS_PORT_READ) — i.e. it was
##              entirely non-functional and several paths fired dangerous
##              port-I/O / mmap / DMA syscalls.  Rewrote to use std::fs for
##              stat/lstat/readlink/link/symlink/unlink/rename (all route to
##              native syscalls via posix libc) and thin extern "C" bindings to
##              the posix statvfs/mkfifo/utimensat symbols for the three ops std
##              lacks.  Unix-only paths gated #[cfg(unix)] with inert host stubs;
##              84 host tests pass, builds clean for x86_64-ouros.  (Earlier note
##              had only flagged the dead-code clock helper at 228->14; the real
##              breakage was the whole filesystem-syscall block.)
##    * dig, rsync, scp, screen, tcpdump — monotonic 30->10 (one-line const;
##              they already used the correct no-arg calling convention).
##    * ntpd  (FIXED 2026-05-30) — read via SYS_CLOCK_REALTIME=14, step via
##              SYS_CLOCK_SETTIME=15 (read abs ns, add correction, write back),
##              slew via SYS_CLOCK_ADJTIME=16 (race-free relative delta).  T1/T4
##              now carry microsecond precision (read_unix_secs_micros), and
##              BOTH apply paths (ntpdate + daemon) work in ns end-to-end,
##              fixing the whole-second truncation that discarded every
##              sub-second correction.  Removed now-dead write_system_time.
##    * hwclock (FIXED 2026-05-30) — read via SYS_CLOCK_REALTIME=14 (btime+uptime
##              kept as a fallback for uninitialised timekeeping), set via
##              SYS_CLOCK_SETTIME=15.  Was reading/writing /proc/time both ways.
##  REMAINING (still broken, NOT yet fixed):
##    * Implement /proc/time in procfs as a convenience read-only mirror
##      (optional) — but the *control* path must be the syscalls, not /proc.
##  CAP_SYS_TIME enforcement (FIXED 2026-05-30): sys_clock_settime and
##  sys_clock_adjtime now call require_clock_authority() before touching any
##  state, rejecting non-root callers with PermissionDenied.  Kernel/bare tasks
##  (caller_pid None or pid 0) bypass.  Currently a no-op because all processes
##  run as uid 0 during early development, but it becomes load-bearing the
##  moment a login service assigns non-root credentials.  NOTE: ideally this
##  would key off a per-process CAP_SYS_TIME bit rather than uid==0, but the
##  PCB has no POSIX-capability bitmask yet (ProcessCredentials is just
##  uid/gid/groups); root-equals-CAP_SYS_TIME matches the documented model and
##  is the correct interim. TRIGGER to revisit: when the PCB gains a real POSIX
##  capability set.
##  ALSO STILL OPEN: a broader userspace-ABI audit.  Now that std is known
##  to work via the posix libc layer, the shared-`oursys`-crate idea (option
##  B) is mostly MOOT for the std binaries — the right fix is to delete their
##  hand-rolled raw-syscall wrappers and call std (and extern "C" posix
##  symbols for the few ops std lacks), exactly as nmap and stat now do.  A
##  shared crate is only worth it for the genuinely no_std bare-metal
##  binaries that cannot link std.
##  nmap (FIXED 2026-05-30) — had SYS_WRITE=1 (=SYS_EXIT, terminated the
##    process on first output!) and SYS_EXIT=60 (=SYS_SYSCTL_GET then loop{}
##    hang); migrated to std::io / std::fs::File / std::process::exit.
##  ===================================================================
##  USERSPACE-ABI AUDIT (done 2026-05-30) — 55 tools hand-roll inline-asm
##  syscalls; cross-checked every `const SYS_* = N` against the authoritative
##  kernel/src/syscall/number.rs.  Authoritative reference numbers used:
##    EXIT=1 TASK_ID=2 CLOCK_MONOTONIC=10 SLEEP=11 CLOCK_REALTIME=14
##    CLOCK_SETTIME=15 CLOCK_ADJTIME=16 IRQ_REGISTER=30 IRQ_WAIT=31
##    DMA_DETACH=49 SYSCTL_GET=60 SYSCTL_SET=61 CONSOLE_WRITE=100
##    CONSOLE_READ_CHAR=101 CHANNEL_CREATE=200 CHANNEL_SEND=201
##    CHANNEL_RECV=202 CHANNEL_TRY_RECV=203 CHANNEL_CLOSE=204
##    PROCESS_SPAWN=500 PROCESS_ID=502 PROCESS_KILL=506 THREAD_SUSPEND=513
##    THREAD_RESUME=514 FS_READ_FILE=600 FS_WRITE_FILE=601 FS_DELETE=602
##    FS_STAT=606 FS_STATVFS=608 FS_OPEN=610 FS_CLOSE=611 FS_READ=612
##    FS_WRITE=613 FS_RENAME=616 FS_SET_OWNER=630 FS_SET_PERMS=631
##    FS_SET_TIMES=632 FS_SYMLINK=637 FS_READLINK=638 FS_LSTAT=639
##    FS_SEEK_DATA=650 FS_SEEK_HOLE=651 TCP_CONNECT=800 TCP_SEND=801
##    TCP_RECV=802 TCP_CLOSE=803 TCP_BIND=804 TCP_ACCEPT=805
##    TCP_CLOSE_LISTENER=806 TCP_PEER_ADDR=808 UDP_BIND=810 UDP_SEND=811
##    UDP_RECV=812 UDP_CLOSE=813 DNS_RESOLVE=820 DNS_REVERSE_RESOLVE=821
##    ICMP_PING=830 ICMP_PING_WAIT=831 NET_IF_INFO=842 ARP_TABLE=843
##    TCP_POLL_STATUS=845 UDP_RX_READY=847 TCP_SET_NODELAY=850 TCP_SHUTDOWN=855
##  Note: there is NO SYS_NET_IOCTL, NO SYS_FS_IOCTL/FORMAT/VERIFY/REPAIR/
##  STATFS, NO SYS_MOUNT/UMOUNT, NO SYS_CHOWN/CHMOD/CHROOT/CHDIR/IOCTL,
##  NO SYS_DRM_IOCTL, NO Linux-style READ/WRITE/OPEN/CLOSE/STAT/MKDIR/etc.
##  in the native ABI.  Tools assuming these are simply broken.
##
##  VERDICT PER TOOL:
##   OK (numbers correct, no change needed):
##     ssh, nc, wget, ftpd, inetd, sshd, ping, traceroute, kill, pgrep,
##     htop, ntpd, hwclock, at, date, rsync, scp, tcpdump, mount-of-channels
##     tools using only channel/service/process numbers that match.
##   CATASTROPHIC (use 1=EXIT as WRITE → process dies on first output, and/or
##   0=YIELD as READ, 60=SYSCTL_GET as EXIT, 4=? as STAT) — same class as the
##   nmap bug; fix by migrating I/O+exit to std (and correct any remaining
##   network numbers):
##     [x] arp  (READ=0 WRITE=1 OPEN=2 CLOSE=3 EXIT=60; ARP_ADD=840=TCP_LIST,
##           ARP_DEL=841 ARP_PROBE=842=NET_IF_INFO IFMAC=843=ARP_TABLE — the
##           arp control syscalls it wants don't exist; only ARP_TABLE=843
##           (read) exists) — FIXED, see PROGRESS + DESIGN GAP below.
##     jq   (READ=0 WRITE=1 OPEN=2 CLOSE=3 EXIT=60) — pure std rewrite
##     zip  (READ=0 WRITE=1 OPEN=2 CLOSE=3 STAT=4 LSEEK=8 MKDIR=83 GETDENTS=78
##           EXIT=60) — pure std rewrite
##     ssh-keygen (READ=0 WRITE=1 OPEN=2 CLOSE=3 EXIT=60 MKDIR=83
##           GETRANDOM=318 STAT=4) — std for I/O; getrandom via std or posix
##     ftp  (READ=0 WRITE=1 OPEN=2 CLOSE=3 STAT=4 GETCWD=79 CHDIR=80
##           GETDENTS=78; TCP 800-806 are CORRECT, DNS=820 correct) — migrate
##           local file/console I/O to std, keep correct TCP numbers
##     sftp (READ=0 WRITE=1 OPEN=2 CLOSE=3 STAT=4 MKDIR=83 UNLINK=87
##           GETDENTS=78 GETCWD=79 CHDIR=80 RENAME=82 CHMOD=90; TCP_SEND=802
##           RECV=803 CLOSE=804 all OFF BY ONE) — std local I/O + fix TCP
##           numbers (SEND=801 RECV=802 CLOSE=803)
##     telnet (READ=0 WRITE=1; TCP_SEND=802 RECV=803 CLOSE=804 off-by-one;
##           IOCTL=16=CLOCK_ADJTIME) — std stdio + fix TCP + drop/replace ioctl
##     screen (CONSOLE_WRITE=0=YIELD CONSOLE_READ_CHAR=1=EXIT) — should be
##           100/101, or migrate to std stdio; CLOCK_MONOTONIC=10/SPAWN=500 ok
##     [x] stty (was IOCTL=16=CLOCK_ADJTIME CLOSE=3) — FIXED 2026-06-01. The
##           premise that stty "needs a NEW termios syscall" was wrong: the
##           posix libc ALREADY exposes a real ioctl() symbol (posix/src/ioctl.rs)
##           that dispatches TCGETS/TCSETS/TIOCGWINSZ/TIOCSWINSZ to the kernel
##           tty path, plus a close() symbol. stty is a std binary that links
##           the sysroot libc, so the proper fix (matching the `stat` pattern)
##           is to bind those C symbols via `unsafe extern "C"` (cfg(unix), with
##           inert host stubs for cfg(not(unix)) test builds) and drop the
##           hand-rolled raw `syscall` wrappers entirely. The posix Termios /
##           Winsize structs are #[repr(C)] with identical layout to stty's
##           (NCCS=32), so the pointers are ABI-compatible. This removes the
##           harmful path where every termios call fired SYS_CLOCK_ADJTIME=16
##           with the struct pointer reinterpreted as a signed-ns clock delta.
##           checks clean for x86_64-ouros; my edited region is clippy-clean.
##           NOTE (RESOLVED 2026-06-01): the pre-existing pervasive
##           clippy::pedantic debt in userspace/stty (unreadable_literal,
##           similar_names, doc_markdown "OurOS", struct_field_names) is now
##           handled by adopting the workspace lint policy — stty (and 14
##           sibling userspace tools) now use `[lints] workspace = true`, which
##           sets pedantic=warn so the crate is clippy-clean (warnings only).
##           See the "15 userspace tools" FIXED entry near the top of this file.
##   WRONG NETWORK NUMBERS (TCP send/recv/close off by one: they use
##   SEND=802 RECV=803 CLOSE=804 instead of 801/802/803):
##     [x] curl, dig, whois — VERIFIED FIXED 2026-06-01 (spot-checked the
##           SYS_TCP_*/SYS_UDP_* consts: curl/whois use SEND=801 RECV=802
##           CLOSE=803; dig uses TCP 801/802/803 and UDP_BIND=810 SEND=811
##           RECV=812). Also verified sftp/telnet TCP consts are now 801/802/803
##           (the off-by-one flagged earlier is resolved). These were corrected
##           in an earlier session; the audit verdict above was stale.
##   NO SUCH SYSCALL — these assume syscalls that don't exist; needs design
##   decision on what the real net/fs-admin ABI is before they can work:
##     dhcpcd fw ifconfig ip nft route  (all NET_IOCTL=810 = UDP_BIND — there
##       is no net-ioctl syscall; net config likely must go via NET_IF_INFO=842
##       / ARP_TABLE=843 / a new syscall set — DESIGN GAP)
##     diskutil (FS_IOCTL=650=FS_SEEK_DATA FORMAT=651=FS_SEEK_HOLE VERIFY/
##       REPAIR/TRIM/STATFS 652-655 unassigned)
##     [x] df  (FS_STAT=650=FS_SEEK_DATA — should be FS_STATVFS=608) — MIS-
##       CLASSIFIED: FS_STATVFS=608 EXISTS with a live handler, so df was
##       fixable NOW (not a design gap).  FIXED — see PROGRESS below.
##     fsck  (FS_VERIFY=652 FS_REPAIR=653 unassigned — no fsck syscall)
##     mkfs  (FS_FORMAT=651=FS_SEEK_HOLE — no format syscall)
##     mount (MOUNT=620=FS_TRASH_RESTORE UMOUNT=621=FS_TRASH_EMPTY — no
##       mount/umount syscall in ABI)
##     [x] chown (CHOWN=30=IRQ_REGISTER CHMOD=31=IRQ_WAIT — should be
##       FS_SET_OWNER=630 / FS_SET_PERMS=631) — MIS-CLASSIFIED: those fs-admin
##       syscalls (628/630/631) EXIST with live handlers, so chown/chmod were
##       fixable now, NOT a design gap.  FIXED — see PROGRESS below.
##     chroot (CHROOT=61=SYSCTL_SET CHDIR=49=DMA_DETACH SETUID=105 SETGID=106
##       SETGROUPS=116 — none exist as named; needs proper process-cred ABI)
##     [x] monctl (DRM_IOCTL=850=TCP_SET_NODELAY — no DRM ioctl syscall) —
##       the SYS_DRM_* family (1000-1060) exists but is compositor primitives
##       (GEM/framebuffer/mode-info), NOT DPMS/backlight; 850 is TCP_SET_NODELAY.
##       FIXED by removing the harmful raw-syscall path and using sysfs (the
##       interface monctl already used for reads).  See PROGRESS below; DPMS
##       idle-timeout policy remains a display-server DESIGN GAP.
##   MINOR WRONG (channel close off by one):
##     [x] logind, powerctl, service (CHANNEL_CLOSE=203=CHANNEL_TRY_RECV —
##       should be 204; CHANNEL_OPEN=200 maps to CHANNEL_CREATE which is fine).
##       Verified SHUTDOWN=90/REBOOT=91 do NOT exist (90/91 unassigned) — see
##       PROGRESS + power-management DESIGN GAP below.
##   [x] lsmod (INIT_MODULE=150 DELETE_MODULE=151 — VERIFIED these are
##       unassigned on OurOS; there is no module ABI because OurOS is a
##       microkernel.  See PROGRESS + kernel-module DESIGN GAP below.)
##
##  FIX ORDER (this pass): catastrophic std-capable tools first (jq, zip,
##  ssh-keygen — pure std rewrites), then off-by-one network const fixes
##  (curl, dig, whois), then the mixed local-I/O+network tools (ftp, sftp,
##  telnet, screen).  The "NO SUCH SYSCALL" group is a DESIGN GAP — those
##  tools need the kernel to actually expose mount/net-ioctl/fs-admin/chown
##  syscalls (or a posix-layer route) before they can be fixed; documented
##  here, deferred until that ABI exists.  TRIGGER for the deferred group:
##  when the corresponding kernel syscalls land (check roadmap for
##  net-config / mount / fs-admin syscall tasks).
##
##  AUDIT CONCLUSION (2026-05-31): re-swept the "NO SUCH SYSCALL" group after
##  discovering the fs-admin syscalls (FS_METADATA=628, FS_SET_OWNER=630,
##  FS_SET_PERMS=631, FS_STATVFS=608) actually exist with live handlers.  THREE
##  entries were mis-classified and are now FIXED: chown/chmod, df, and monctl
##  (monctl had a real alternative — sysfs — so it was fixable even though no
##  DPMS/backlight syscall exists).  The remaining SIX are CONFIRMED genuine
##  design gaps — each verified absent from kernel/src/syscall/number.rs:
##    * net-config (dhcpcd, fw, ifconfig, ip, nft, route): all use
##      SYS_NET_IOCTL=810 (=UDP_BIND) for interface/route/DNS/firewall WRITES.
##      No net-config write syscall exists; only NET_IF_INFO=842 / ARP_TABLE=843
##      (read-only).  Unlike monctl there is no sysfs write path present, so
##      neutering the bad syscall would just make every command fail with no
##      alternative.  Needs a real net-config ABI or a network-manager daemon
##      over IPC.  (A future partial win: wire the READ paths — ifconfig with no
##      args, `ip addr show`, `route -n` — to NET_IF_INFO=842.)
##      PRECISE HARM (traced 2026-06-01): sys_udp_bind (handlers.rs:6954) reads
##      arg0 as a u16 port, requires a Socket WRITE cap, rejects port==0, and
##      otherwise binds a fresh UDP socket returning a handle.  So today these
##      tools don't corrupt anything, but if the caller holds a Socket WRITE
##      cap they silently bind+leak a UDP socket on whatever low port their
##      first numeric arg maps to (and the "success" misleads the user into
##      thinking the interface/route/firewall change applied).  Without the cap
##      they fail with a permission error.  Either way the intended net-config
##      operation never happens — confirming this is a no-op-at-best design gap,
##      NOT a quick fix.  Do not neuter autonomously: the right fix (real
##      net-config syscall family vs. a netmgr IPC daemon) is a human decision.
##    * mount/umount: no MOUNT/UMOUNT syscall (the numbers it used, 620/621, are
##      FS_TRASH_RESTORE/EMPTY).
##    * mkfs/fsck/diskutil: no FS_FORMAT/FS_VERIFY/FS_REPAIR/FS_TRIM syscall
##      (650-655 are SEEK_DATA/SEEK_HOLE + unassigned).
##    * chroot: no CHROOT/CHDIR/SETUID/SETGID/SETGROUPS syscall — needs a proper
##      process-credential + filesystem-root ABI.
##    * stty: no SYS_IOCTL/termios path (see terminal-attr DESIGN GAP below).
##  So the deferred group is now exactly these six; no further mis-classifications
##  remain.  TRIGGER unchanged: revisit when the matching kernel ABI lands.
##

##           OPEN=2 CLOSE=3 EXIT=60 and ARP_ADD=840 ARP_DEL=841 ARP_PROBE=842
##           IFMAC=843 — every one of those numbers means something else on
##           OurOS (840=TCP_LIST, 842=NET_IF_INFO, 843=ARP_TABLE) and WRITE=1

##   [x] chown/chmod — MIS-CLASSIFIED in the "NO SUCH SYSCALL" group above:
##           the old code used CHOWN=30/CHMOD=31 (which are IRQ_REGISTER/

##           handlers — SYS_FS_SET_OWNER=630, SYS_FS_SET_PERMS=631,
##           SYS_FS_METADATA=628.  So this was fixable now, not a design gap.
##           Rewrote the syscall layer on the real ABI:
##             * syscall4 wrapper with arg3 in r10 (the syscall insn clobbers
##               rcx with the return address, so arg3 CANNOT go in rcx);
##               syscall3 forwards with a0..a2 + zero a4.
##             * do_chown -> syscall4(SET_OWNER, ptr, len, uid, gid); uid/gid
##               of u32::MAX = "leave unchanged" (resolved by Vfs::set_owner).
##             * do_chmod -> syscall3(SET_PERMS, ptr, len, mode & 0o7777).
##             * Replaced the bogus Linux-errno mapper with kernel_error_to_string
##               mapping OurOS KernelError discriminants (-500 = NotFound, etc.,
##               NOT ENOENT).
##           Used SYS_FS_METADATA=628 (64-byte buffer; uid@48 gid@52 perms@56,
##           all LE) to implement the previously-stubbed features PROPERLY:
##             * --reference now reads the ref file's owner/mode (was: "not yet
##               supported").
##             * symbolic chmod (u+x etc.) now applies deltas to the file's
##               ACTUAL current mode (was: assumed base 0o000, so '-' on set
##               bits silently no-op'd).
##             * --from filter now verifies real current ownership before
##               changing (was: a no-op placeholder that changed unconditionally).
##             * -c/--changes and -v/--verbose now report accurately (compare
##               old vs new), distinguishing "changed" from "retained as".
##           parse_metadata_buffer split out so it's host-unit-testable; the
##           syscall fns are #[cfg(target_arch="x86_64")] with non-x86_64 host

##           39-test module (octal/symbolic mode parse+apply, owner-spec parse,
##           group-table/uid-gid resolution, --from parse, metadata-buffer parse,
##           error mapping, formatting).  Clippy-clean on both host and ouros
##           targets; build-ouros clean.
##           KNOWN LIMITATION: -h/--no-dereference cannot be honored — the VFS
##           SET_OWNER path resolves symlinks (resolve_follow) and there is no
##           lchown-equivalent syscall yet, so chown -h now WARNS that the target
##           will be affected rather than silently chowning the wrong inode.
