##   9. KILL accepts every signal in 1..=NSIG (=64).  sys_kill
##      delegates to handlers::sys_signal_send, which calls
##      signal::classify_post(target, sig) — that function knows the
##      POSIX default-action table (Terminate / Drop / Stop / Continue /
##      Deliver-to-handler) and routes accordingly.  sig=0 and
##      sig>NSIG return -EINVAL.  Limitation: job-control signals
##      (SIGSTOP / SIGCONT / SIGTSTP / SIGTTIN / SIGTTOU) are silently
##      dropped — we don't have job control / process stopping, so
##      classify_post resolves them as PostDecision::Drop.  Real Linux
##      programs that block on SIGSTOP/SIGCONT for foreground/
##      background terminal control won't behave correctly, but most
##      non-shell programs are unaffected.
##
## TESTING:
##   - linux::self_test() at boot exercises: errno mapping (16 KernelError
##     variants); linux_from_native round-trip; unknown nr -> -ENOSYS;
##     sched_yield; write to bad fd -> -EBADF; writev bad iovcnt ->
##     -EINVAL; clock_gettime bad clk -> -EINVAL; arch_prctl bad code
##     -> -EINVAL; LinuxTimespec to_nanos / from_nanos roundtrip;
##     LinuxTimespec rejects negative tv_sec and tv_nsec >= 1e9;
##     kernel_error_from_code inverse of code() for all mapped variants;
##     direct dispatch_linux invocation for getpid, gettid, getuid,
##     getgid.  Fd-table-backed syscalls (read/close/dup/fcntl/lseek)
##     correctly return -EBADF when the caller has no fd table; dup3
##     with oldfd==newfd returns -EINVAL; openat with a non-AT_FDCWD
##     dirfd returns -ENOSYS; translate_open_flags maps O_RDONLY,
##     O_WRONLY|O_CREAT|O_TRUNC, and O_RDWR|O_APPEND correctly.
##   - linux_fd::self_test() at boot exercises: empty / with_stdio
##     construction; install_lowest after stdio gives 3,4,5;
##     install_lowest_from(10, ...) honours the min_fd; lookup OOB
##     returns None; is_handle_referenced semantics; dup_lowest clones
##     entry and clears FD_CLOEXEC; dup2 closes prior occupant and
##     returns it; dup2(fd,fd) is a no-op; take removes entry;
##     set_fd_flags / set_status_flags preserve O_ACCMODE;
##     take_cloexec_entries returns exactly the FD_CLOEXEC'd entries
##     and leaves non-cloexec fds intact; ensure_stdio refills missing
##     stdio slots with Console entries but does NOT overwrite a
##     non-Console fd sitting at 0/1/2.
##   - dispatch_linux_with_frame routing: non-frame syscalls return
##     None; EXECVE from a contextless self-test task returns
##     Some(-ESRCH) (no owning process to exec); FORK / VFORK from a
##     contextless self-test task return a negative errno (proves
##     routing reaches fork_process); CLONE with thread-creation
##     bits but child_stack=0 returns Some(-ENOSYS); CLONE with bad
##     stack and no CLONE_VM/CLONE_THREAD returns Some(-ENOSYS);
##     full pthread-style CLONE (CLONE_VM | CLONE_THREAD | ... with
##     non-zero child_stack) reaches thread_clone::clone_thread which
##     returns Some(-ESRCH) when there's no owning process — proves
##     the new thread-creation route is wired (NOT -ENOSYS).
##   - read_user_cstr(NULL, _) returns Err(EFAULT) without touching
##     userspace; read_user_ptr_array(NULL, _) returns Ok(empty) (how
##     glibc passes an argv-less execve).
##   - thread_clone::self_test() at boot exercises: build_register_image
##     slot layout (RIP/RFLAGS/RSP/RDI/R9/R15/FS_BASE positions);
##     RFLAGS substitution (zero -> 0x202); CLEAR_CHILD_TID register
##     and clear (register-to-0 removes the entry per Linux
##     set_tid_address semantics); on_thread_exit_hook is a no-op for
##     unregistered tasks; clone_thread rejects child_stack==0 with
##     KernelError::InvalidArgument BEFORE looking up the pid.
##   - rt_sigreturn via dispatch_linux_with_frame with a misaligned
##     user_rsp returns -EFAULT (both candidate ucontext addresses
##     fail the alignment gate before any unsafe deref).  user_rip is
##     left untouched on the failure path so userspace can recover.
##   - Linux-sigaction table round-trip: a fresh pid reads back
##     SIG_DFL/0/0/0; storing a non-default entry round-trips; per-
##     signal independence (writing signal 11 leaves signal 10
##     unaffected); on_exec preserves SIG_IGN handlers but zeros their
##     flags/restorer/mask while clearing caught (non-DFL/IGN) entries
##     back to defaults; on_fork copies the parent table to a fresh
##     child pid; on_exit removes every entry so a re-read returns
##     defaults again.
##   - dispatch_linux rt_sigaction validation: sig=0, sig=65, and
##     sigsetsize=7 each return -EINVAL without mutating any state.
##   - mprotect argument validation via dispatch_linux: zero length
##     succeeds as no-op; unknown prot bits, misaligned addr, and
##     kernel-space addr each return their respective errnos (EINVAL
##     / EINVAL / EFAULT).
##   - mprotect_flush_range routing: degenerate (end<=start) is a
##     no-op; ranges <= 64 4 KiB pages bump tlb::stats().range_flushes;
##     ranges > 64 pages bump tlb::stats().full_flushes; tested with
##     kernel-VA dummy addresses since the function only does TLB
##     work, never page-table walks.
##   - clone(SIGCHLD | CLONE_VFORK) via dispatch_linux_with_frame
##     reaches fork::fork_process (returns ESRCH in the contextless
##     test task) — proves CLONE_VFORK is no longer rejected at the
##     flag check.  clone(SIGCHLD | CLONE_PARENT/CLONE_NEWNS/
##     CLONE_PTRACE) each still return -ENOSYS.
##   - kill signal-number gate via dispatch_linux: sig=0 (existence
##     probe) MUST NOT return -EINVAL (expects ESRCH for a probe pid
##     that doesn't exist); sig=65 and sig=u64::MAX each return
##     -EINVAL; sig in {9, 15, 17, 64} each progress past the gate
##     (i.e. don't return -EINVAL, proving the linux ABI accepts the
##     full 1..=NSIG range and not just SIGKILL/SIGTERM).
##   - madvise: len=0 succeeds even with bogus addr+advice; known
##     hints 0/1/2/3/MADV_DONTNEED(4)/MADV_FREE(8)/MADV_COLLAPSE(25)
##     return 0; MADV_HWPOISON(100) and MADV_SOFT_OFFLINE(101) return
##     -EPERM (privileged on real Linux, never exposed here);
##     advice=26 (between documented max and HWPOISON) returns
##     -EINVAL; misaligned addr with nonzero len returns -EINVAL;
##     kernel-space addr with nonzero len returns -ENOMEM.
##   - encode_linux_wstatus pure-function: normal exit code 42 ->
##     WIFEXITED true (low 7 bits == 0) and WEXITSTATUS == 42; kernel
##     exit code 128+15 -> WTERMSIG == 15 and WIFSIGNALED true; any
##     ExitInfo.crash.is_some() -> wstatus low 7 bits == 11 (SIGSEGV).
##   - rlimit_default pure-function: RLIMIT_STACK (3) is (8 MiB,
##     u64::MAX), RLIMIT_NOFILE (7) is (1024, 4096), RLIMIT_CORE
##     (4) is (0, 0), RLIMIT_CPU (0) is (u64::MAX, u64::MAX).
##   - prlimit64 dispatch: resource == 16 and u64::MAX both return
##     -EINVAL; cross-pid query (pid=1 with caller_pid=0/None)
##     returns -EPERM; pid=0 with both NULL pointers is a 0-return
##     no-op success.
##   - wait4 dispatch via dispatch_linux: unknown option bits return
##     -EINVAL before any reap attempt; wait-any WNOHANG from
##     contextless test task does NOT return -EINVAL (proves the
##     options validator didn't reject the legal WNOHANG=1 bit);
##     wait-specific WNOHANG for fake pid 0xDEAD_BEEF returns a
##     negative errno other than -EINVAL (proves we reached
##     try_reap's "not a child" path -> ECHILD).  Bad wstatus / rusage
##     pointer EFAULT is NOT tested at boot because
##     validate_user_write has a documented kernel-context bypass
##     that makes it impossible to observe — the shared validation
##     infrastructure is exercised by every other syscall and will
##     EFAULT on bad pointers from real userspace.
##   - Cross-ABI dispatch routing in entry.rs is *structurally* tested
##     by the AbiMode default-Native path that every existing native
##     test hits.  The Linux path will get end-to-end coverage when an
##     actual Linux binary can be loaded.
##
## NEXT STEPS (in priority order):
##   1. GETRANDOM CSPRNG — DONE.  sys_getrandom now calls
##      crate::rng::fill (ChaCha20-based CSPRNG seeded at boot from
##      RDSEED/RDRAND/HPET/TSC).  The previous xorshift64-from-TSC
##      stream is gone.  Flags (GRND_NONBLOCK / GRND_RANDOM /
##      GRND_INSECURE) are accepted but ignored — we never block and
##      we don't distinguish urandom/random sources.
##   2. Cross-CPU TLB shootdown for mprotect — DONE.  sys_mprotect
##      now batches all PTE updates and ends with a single
##      mprotect_flush_range() call that delegates to
##      crate::tlb::flush_range / flush_all.  Both are SMP-aware (send
##      an IPI to every other online CPU and spin until they ack),
##      so a sibling pthread running on another core cannot observe
##      stale permissions past the mprotect return.  Strategy:
##        - len <= 64 4 KiB pages -> flush_range (one IPI, N invlpgs)
##        - len  > 64 4 KiB pages -> flush_all (one IPI, CR3 reload)
##      Threshold 64 ≈ Linux's tlb_single_page_flush_ceiling (33),
##      bumped up to 64 because our hardware page is the same 4 KiB
##      but our frames are 16 KiB so the average mprotect covers a
##      smaller page-count for a given byte size.  Boot self-test
##      observes crate::tlb::stats() delta to prove small ranges take
##      the range path and large ranges promote to full-flush.
##   3. Real PROT_NONE.  Requires VMA tracking so the page-fault
##      handler can distinguish "mapped but PROT_NONE" from "never
##      mapped".  Today PROT_NONE is approximated as read-only +
##      no-execute, which is wrong for any program that intentionally
##      uses PROT_NONE as a guard page or trap region.
##   4. Honour brk properly.  brk's no-op is acceptable because glibc
##      malloc falls back to mmap.
##   4b. sigaction sa_mask / sa_flags / SA_RESTART — STORAGE DONE.
##      kernel/src/syscall/linux.rs now keeps a per-process per-signal
##      table (linux_sigaction_table) of the full Linux struct sigaction
##      { sa_handler, sa_flags, sa_restorer, sa_mask }.  rt_sigaction
##      writes the requested entry (rejecting unknown sa_flags bits via
##      sa_flags::MASK, sig=0 / sig>NSIG / sigsetsize != 0 && != 8 with
##      EINVAL, and SIGKILL/SIGSTOP as SET targets with EINVAL) and
##      copies the previous entry out to oldact before overwriting.
##      Fork copies the parent table to the child; exec preserves
##      SIG_IGN entries (but clears flags/restorer/mask) and resets
##      every caught entry to SIG_DFL per POSIX; process exit clears
##      the table.  Boot self-tests cover round-trip, per-signal
##      independence, on_fork / on_exec / on_exit, plus the EINVAL
##      validation paths.
##      Limitation: stored sa_flags / sa_mask are NOT yet consumed at
##      delivery time.  deliver_pending_signal still uses the legacy
##      proc::signal trampoline (which rt_sigaction continues to sync
##      for catchable handlers, so basic SIGINT/SIGTERM keep working),
##      so SA_NODEFER / SA_RESETHAND / SA_RESTART / sa_mask blocking
##      and SA_SIGINFO siginfo_t* delivery are all no-ops until the
##      Linux-shaped rt_sigframe delivery work (item 6 below) lands.
##      sys_rt_sigaction's oldact return value IS truthful now even
##      for stored-but-unused fields, so glibc that round-trips via
##      sigaction-old==sigaction-new sees consistent state.
##   5. RT_SIGRETURN — DONE (via native restore path).  Linux's
##      rt_sigreturn(2) is now routed through
##      dispatch_linux_with_frame and reuses sys_signal_return_with_
##      frame to restore the saved SignalContext.  Both calling
##      conventions are supported: direct sigreturn from the handler
##      (ctx at user_rsp + 8) and via SA_RESTORER (ctx at user_rsp).
##      Defensive alignment check on the candidate ucontext pointer
##      keeps us out of Rust's debug-mode misaligned-deref panic when
##      validate_user_read short-circuits in kernel context.
##      Limitation: signal delivery (proc::signal::deliver_pending_
##      signal) writes our *native* SignalContext on the user stack,
##      not Linux's ucontext_t.  Real Linux programs using a glibc
##      that walks the ucontext at known field offsets won't work
##      until delivery emits a Linux-shaped rt_sigframe — tracked as
##      a follow-up below.
##   6. Linux-shaped signal delivery frame.  Today
##      deliver_pending_signal writes a native SignalContext for both
##      ABIs.  For full Linux compat the delivery path needs to know
##      the calling ABI and emit either:
##        - native SignalContext (current behavior, for our ABI), or
##        - Linux rt_sigframe { ucontext_t uc; siginfo_t info; ... }
##          with mcontext_t.gregs[*] populated per AMD64 SysV.
##      rt_sigreturn would then need to detect which layout is on the
##      stack (probably via a magic / sentinel field) and restore
##      accordingly.  Acceptable to defer until real Linux binaries
##      are running.
##   7. CLONE_VFORK — DONE-with-approximation.  linux_clone now
##      accepts clone(CLONE_VFORK | SIGCHLD, ...) and degenerates it
##      to a plain fork.  Linux's vfork() guarantees (a) parent blocks
##      until child execve's or _exit's, and (b) child shares parent's
##      address space until then.  (a) is a performance hint per POSIX
##      ("vfork == fork is permitted"), not a correctness requirement
##      — every conformant caller of vfork must work against a plain
##      fork.  (b) we don't honour, but CoW gives the child a logically
##      identical address space.  Same approximation as the dedicated
##      VFORK syscall (which has worked this way since the initial
##      Linux ABI port).  Real parent-blocking vfork semantics are
##      tracked as a future enhancement but are low-value since
##      conformant callers work either way.
##      CLONE_PARENT / CLONE_NEWNS / CLONE_PTRACE continue to return
##      -ENOSYS — they need infrastructure (PID reparenting, mount
##      namespaces, ptrace lineage) we don't have yet.
##      Boot self-test exercises both: clone(SIGCHLD | CLONE_VFORK)
##      no longer returns -ENOSYS (it reaches fork::fork_process and
##      bails with ESRCH in the contextless test task); clone with
##      any of CLONE_PARENT / CLONE_NEWNS / CLONE_PTRACE still
##      returns -ENOSYS.
##   8. MADVISE — DONE-as-advisory-no-op.  sys_madvise validates
##      addr alignment, frame-rounds len, range-checks against
##      USER_SPACE_END, then accepts all documented Linux MADV_*
##      hints in 0..=25 (NORMAL/RANDOM/SEQUENTIAL/WILLNEED/DONTNEED/
##      FREE/REMOVE/DONTFORK/DOFORK/MERGEABLE/UNMERGEABLE/HUGEPAGE/
##      NOHUGEPAGE/DONTDUMP/DODUMP/WIPEONFORK/KEEPONFORK/COLD/
##      PAGEOUT/POPULATE_READ/POPULATE_WRITE/DONTNEED_LOCKED/
##      COLLAPSE) returning 0.  HWPOISON (100) and SOFT_OFFLINE (101)
##      return -EPERM (privileged memory-failure injection that we
##      don't expose).  Unknown advice returns -EINVAL.
##      Rationale: glibc/jemalloc/tcmalloc/mimalloc call
##      MADV_DONTNEED on every free() to release pages back to the
##      kernel.  Returning -ENOSYS made every free() syscall-and-fail
##      while RSS grew unbounded.  Treating advisory hints as a no-op
##      is always semantically valid (Linux is allowed to ignore any
##      MADV_* hint) and lets allocators stop spamming the syscall.
##      Limitation: we don't actually free anonymous frames on
##      MADV_DONTNEED yet — that needs VMA tracking to know what's
##      anonymous vs file-backed.  Tracked in item 3 (PROT_NONE
##      with VMA layer).  Until then, MADV_DONTNEED leaves the pages
##      committed; future allocator activity re-uses them in place
##      rather than re-zero-faulting.
##   9. WAIT4 — DONE.  sys_wait4 is wired through dispatch_linux,
##      validates the options bitmap (WNOHANG=1, WUNTRACED=2,
##      WCONTINUED=8; unknown bits -> EINVAL), pre-validates wstatus
##      and rusage user pointers, then routes:
##        - pid > 0  -> pcb::try_reap(parent, target)
##        - pid <= 0 -> pcb::try_reap_any(parent)
##      and threads through the same wait-task registration / re-check
##      / block_current loop as sys_process_wait when WNOHANG is
##      clear.  WNOHANG with no ready child returns 0 (Linux
##      convention).  PermissionDenied / NoSuchProcess from try_reap
##      collapse to -ECHILD (Linux: "not your child" and "no such
##      child" are both ECHILD).
##      encode_linux_wstatus translates ExitInfo to Linux <sys/wait.h>
##      encoding: normal exit code C -> (C&0xff)<<8 (WIFEXITED+
##      WEXITSTATUS); native exit_code in 128..=255 (our kill
##      convention) -> sig&0x7f (WIFSIGNALED+WTERMSIG); crash -> 11
##      (SIGSEGV).  WUNTRACED/WCONTINUED are accepted-but-ignored
##      because we have no process-stop mechanism — there are no
##      stopped or continued children to report.
##      Rusage is zeroed when the user pointer is non-null (we don't
##      track per-process resource usage yet; programs that consume
##      ru_utime/ru_stime see zero CPU time but don't crash).
##      Limitation: crash -> SIGSEGV is a heuristic.  Most crashes
##      ARE page faults so SIGSEGV is correct most of the time, but
##      a DivideError should map to SIGFPE, InvalidOpcode to SIGILL,
##      etc.  Future enhancement: read CrashInfo.exception_code and
##      map to the right Linux signal number.  Also: process groups
##      aren't implemented (pid==0 and pid<-1 both degrade to
##      "any child"), which is conformant but loses fidelity for
##      shells that wait on a process group.
##  10. PRLIMIT64 — DONE with static defaults.  sys_prlimit64
##      validates resource in 0..=15 (otherwise EINVAL), permits
##      target pid 0 or pid == caller (otherwise EPERM — Linux
##      requires CAP_SYS_RESOURCE for cross-process limits), pre-
##      validates new_limit / old_limit user pointers (each 16
##      bytes: rlim_cur, rlim_max as u64), accepts the new limit
##      as a no-op, and writes a compiled-in default to old_limit
##      via rlimit_default(resource).
##      Defaults that matter for glibc / typical programs:
##        - RLIMIT_STACK = (8 MiB, INFINITY)   sizes glibc's main
##          thread stack correctly
##        - RLIMIT_NOFILE = (1024, 4096)       fits FD_SETSIZE for
##          select(); matches typical Linux distro defaults
##        - RLIMIT_CORE = (0, 0)               we never produce
##          core dumps
##        - RLIMIT_NICE / RLIMIT_RTPRIO = (0, 0)  no nice / RT
##        - everything else = (INFINITY, INFINITY)
##      Limitation: limits are global and read-only.  Per-process
##      storage would let setrlimit honour user changes; today they
##      silently no-op.  This is fine for read-mostly users (glibc
##      sizing its main thread stack from RLIMIT_STACK) but
##      programs that lower a limit then verify it failed (e.g. a
##      sandbox dropping privileges) won't see the lowered value
##      reflected.  Tracked as a future enhancement when a real
##      per-process rlimit store is added.
##  11. RT_SIGPENDING — DONE.  sys_rt_sigpending validates sigsetsize
##      == sizeof(sigset_t) == 8 first (EINVAL otherwise) so a sane
##      libc bug-checks its own assumptions before we touch user
##      memory, validates the user-write range, then copies the
##      caller process's pending-signal bitmap from
##      crate::proc::signal::pending(pid) into the user sigset_t.
##      For tasks with no owning process (kernel self-tests) the
##      pending mask reads back as 0, which matches "no signals
##      pending" — observationally correct.
##  12. TKILL / TGKILL — DONE-with-approximation.  sys_tkill resolves
##      owner_process(tid) and, on ESRCH for non-thread tids,
##      degenerates to sys_kill(pid, sig) with the same sig==0
##      existence-probe semantics.  sys_tgkill additionally verifies
##      that owner_process(tid) == tgid (Linux's race-free tid-reuse
##      check); a mismatch yields ESRCH.  Both wire through
##      dispatch_linux at the new nr::TKILL=200 / nr::TGKILL=234
##      slots.
##      Limitation: we don't have multi-threaded per-thread signal
##      routing yet.  Every signal — whether sent via kill(pid),
##      tkill(tid), or tgkill(tgid,tid) — gets posted to the owning
##      process's single pending mask and delivered to whichever
##      thread of that process happens to be ready.  For single-
##      threaded programs (the common case for early Linux binaries)
##      this is observationally identical to Linux.  For glibc's
##      pthread_kill targeting a specific worker thread of a multi-
##      threaded process, the signal will be delivered, just not
##      necessarily to the requested thread.  Real per-thread
##      delivery is tracked alongside the Linux-shaped rt_sigframe
##      delivery work (item 6) — they touch the same pending-set
##      machinery in proc::signal.
##  13. UMASK — DONE as static-stub.  sys_umask always returns 0o022
##      (the de-facto Linux distro default) and silently discards the
##      requested mask.  Rationale: the PCB doesn't carry per-process
##      umask storage, the VFS doesn't apply umask at create time,
##      and no other kernel code observes the value — so a no-op
##      returning the conventional default is the most useful stub
##      for programs that read-then-restore (`old = umask(0);
##      umask(old);`) or check whether umask is "sane" at startup.
##      Limitation: a program that does `umask(0o077); creat(...);`
##      and then stats the new file will see the kernel-default
##      permissions, not mask-respecting ones.  Tracked as needing
##      per-process umask storage on the PCB plus VFS plumbing to
##      consume it at create time.
##  14. SIGALTSTACK — DONE as disabled-stub.  sys_sigaltstack
##      validates ss/old_ss user pointers (24 bytes: stack_t {ss_sp,
##      ss_flags, padding, ss_size}) when non-NULL, silently
##      discards any input ss, writes ss_flags == SS_DISABLE (= 2)
##      to old_ss to communicate "no alternate stack in effect",
##      and returns 0.
##      Limitation: programs that catch SIGSEGV with SA_ONSTACK to
##      print a backtrace after blowing the main stack will deliver
##      to the already-blown stack and double-fault.  Tracked
##      alongside item 6 (Linux-shaped rt_sigframe delivery) — the
##      signal-delivery path is the same refactor.
##  15. IOCTL — DONE as ENOTTY-everywhere.  sys_ioctl returns
##      -ENOTTY for every (fd, request) pair, which is the
##      semantically correct response for ioctls on non-tty fds.
##      Specifically, isatty(3) is defined as `ioctl(fd, TCGETS,
##      &tio) != -1`, so this stub gives isatty() a clean "0 with
##      errno=ENOTTY" answer — exactly what Linux returns for
##      isatty(stdout) when stdout is a regular file.
##      Limitation: programs that legitimately need ioctl to succeed
##      (e.g. FIONBIO on a socket, though glibc/musl normally use
##      fcntl(F_SETFL, O_NONBLOCK) for this) will hard-fail.  Once
##      we have a real fd table with driver routing, this becomes a
##      per-fd dispatch — the driver decides whether to handle the
##      request and we fall back to ENOTTY only if nobody does.
##  16. PRCTL — DONE for the libc-startup option set.  sys_prctl
##      accepts and returns sensible values for the PR_* options
##      that real Linux startup code hits, and EINVAL for everything
##      else (Linux's documented behaviour for unknown options):
##        - PR_SET_NAME / PR_GET_NAME — accept (drop the name) /
##          zero the user buf.  No per-thread comm storage yet.
##        - PR_SET_PDEATHSIG — accept silently (we don't track
##          parent-death notifications; systemd accepts SET failure
##          but accepting keeps the log quiet).
##        - PR_SET_DUMPABLE / PR_GET_DUMPABLE — SET accepts any
##          value; GET returns 0 (not dumpable — we don't produce
##          core dumps).
##        - PR_SET_KEEPCAPS / PR_GET_KEEPCAPS — accept SET; GET
##          returns 0.  No uid model, so capability preservation
##          across uid change is vacuously satisfied.
##        - PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS / PR_GET_NO_NEW_PRIVS — accept SET;
##          GET returns 1 (the paranoid answer — we don't honour
##          setuid bits so "no new privs" is true by construction).
##        - PR_CAPBSET_READ — return 1 ("cap is in bset") for any
##          capability, since we don't have POSIX-style cap bits.
##          Lets systemd's PR_CAPBSET_DROP loop run without
##          spuriously thinking a cap doesn't exist.
##        - PR_CAPBSET_DROP — silent success.
##      Limitation: PR_SET_NAME / PR_GET_NAME are no-ops; debuggers
##      that inspect /proc/<pid>/comm for thread identification see
##      empty names.  Tracked as needing per-thread name storage on
##      the TCB and a procfs string field.
##  17. PERSONALITY — DONE as static PER_LINUX.  sys_personality
##      returns 0 (PER_LINUX) regardless of input.  Programs query
##      with personality(0xffff_ffff) to verify "are we Linux?";
##      systemd / glibc init paths check this at startup.  Accepts
##      sets without honouring them (Linux ignores most bits anyway).
##  18. GETRESUID / GETRESGID — DONE returning all zeros.  We have
##      no uid model; everything runs as the implicit "root-
##      equivalent" owner of all kernel objects via the capability
##      system.  Reporting ruid==euid==suid==0 lets pre-existing
##      Linux code's geteuid()==0 privilege checks fire the way the
##      program expects.  Validates each non-NULL pointer for
##      writability (4 bytes per uid_t on Linux x86_64) and writes
##      zeros.  NULL pointers are skipped per POSIX.
##      Limitation: any program that drops privileges via setresuid
##      and then verifies the drop by reading back via getresuid
##      will see "uid 0" returned and may refuse to continue.  No
##      such programs are in our early bring-up corpus; future work
##      tracked alongside a real uid model.
##  19. GETRUSAGE / SYSINFO / TIMES — DONE as best-effort stubs.
##      sys_getrusage zeros a 144-byte struct rusage (no per-process
##      CPU time tracking yet).  sys_sysinfo fills in uptime
##      (from timekeeping::uptime_secs) and totalram / freeram (from
##      mm::frame::stats) with mem_unit==1; load averages, swap, and
##      proc counts stay zero.  sys_times zeros the 32-byte tms
##      struct when non-NULL and returns ticks since boot at HZ==100
##      (clock_monotonic / 1e7).
##      Limitation: per-process CPU accounting is not tracked.
##      Programs that profile themselves with getrusage(SELF) and
##      time their own execution will see zero CPU time.  Tracked
##      alongside scheduler-side per-task accounting in todo.txt.
##  20. Process groups & sessions (GETPGRP, GETPGID, SETPGID,
##      GETSID, SETSID) — DONE as "every process is alone".  We
##      don't carry group / session membership on the PCB so the
##      most truthful answer is "pgid == sid == pid" — each process
##      is the leader of its own pgroup and session.  GETPGRP /
##      GETPGID(0) / GETSID(0) return the caller pid; GETPGID(p) /
##      GETSID(p) return p if it exists else ESRCH.  SETPGID
##      rejects negative pgids (EINVAL), accepts everything else as
##      silent success.  SETSID returns the caller pid (per Linux's
##      "new session ID equals caller pid" contract).
##      Limitation: kill(-pgid) for "signal the whole group" won't
##      hit multiple processes — they're all in their own groups.
##      Shell job control (Ctrl-Z, fg/bg) needs real process groups.
##      Tracked alongside session / pgroup infrastructure on the PCB.
##  21. GETPRIORITY / SETPRIORITY — DONE returning 0.  Our scheduler
##      runs strict round-robin within a priority class; nice values
##      are not honoured.  Reporting "nice == 0" (the unbiased
##      default) is the most truthful answer.  which must be in
##      0..=2 (PRIO_PROCESS / PRIO_PGRP / PRIO_USER); larger
##      values return EINVAL per Linux.
##      Limitation: programs that try to raise their own priority
##      with setpriority(-20) won't see preferential scheduling.
##  22. Credential setters (SETUID, SETGID, SETREUID, SETREGID,
##      SETRESUID, SETRESGID, SETFSUID, SETFSGID, GETGROUPS,
##      SETGROUPS) — DONE as silent successes.  We have no
##      UID/GID model — all processes run as the implicit root
##      owner of all kernel objects, mediated by the capability
##      system.  Accepting every credential change as a no-op is
##      consistent with the "everyone's effectively root" stance
##      and friendlier than EPERM (which would break programs
##      that drop privileges as a defense-in-depth measure: they'd
##      refuse to start when setuid(nobody) fails).
##      Limitation: a program that drops to non-root and then
##      audits via getresuid sees uid 0 back (already documented
##      under getresuid/getresgid in item 18) — they might refuse
##      to continue.  No such programs in the early-bring-up corpus.
##  23. CAPGET / CAPSET — DONE for V1/V2/V3 with all-ones caps.
##      sys_capget validates the version field (Linux's documented
##      retry protocol: unknown version returns EINVAL with the
##      hdrp.version rewritten to V3), reads the requested element
##      count (1 for V1, 2 for V2/V3), and writes 0xff into every
##      byte of the datap range — reporting "every capability is
##      effective + permitted + inheritable."  This is the
##      friendliest answer for systemd, Docker, and the like which
##      probe capabilities at startup; reporting "no caps" would
##      make them refuse to do almost anything.
##      sys_capset accepts any well-formed (validated version)
##      request as silent success.
##      Limitation: capabilities don't actually gate any kernel
##      operation today (the kernel-level capability system uses
##      typed handles, not POSIX cap bits).  PR_CAPBSET_DROP /
##      CAPSET combinations that sandboxes use to drop dangerous
##      privileges are observed but not enforced.  Tracked
##      alongside POSIX-cap-style enforcement work in todo.txt.
##  24. Scheduler-policy syscalls (SCHED_GETSCHEDULER /
##      SCHED_SETSCHEDULER / SCHED_GETPARAM / SCHED_SETPARAM /
##      SCHED_GET_PRIORITY_MAX / SCHED_GET_PRIORITY_MIN /
##      SCHED_RR_GET_INTERVAL) — DONE returning the SCHED_OTHER
##      defaults.  Our scheduler is strict priority-round-robin
##      with a kernel-internal priority concept that doesn't map
##      to Linux's policy classes (OTHER/FIFO/RR/BATCH/IDLE/DEADLINE).
##      We report SCHED_OTHER (== 0) for every getscheduler query
##      and accept any policy in 0..=7 as silent success.  Priority
##      bounds match Linux exactly (FIFO/RR: [1, 99]; others: [0, 0])
##      so sanity checks pass.  sched_rr_get_interval reports a
##      100 ms time slice (a typical Linux RR slice).
##      Limitation: setting policy / priority is a no-op; the
##      scheduler still uses its own priority scheme.
##  25. SCHED_GETAFFINITY / SCHED_SETAFFINITY — DONE reporting all
##      online CPUs.  getaffinity bit-fills a cpuset mask from
##      0..N where N = smp::cpu_count(), validates cpusetsize is
##      at least ceil(N/8), and returns the number of bytes written
##      (Linux convention).  setaffinity validates the user range
##      and accepts the mask as silent success.
##      Limitation: affinity is advisory and the scheduler doesn't
##      honour it; getaffinity always reports "all CPUs" even after
##      a successful setaffinity narrowing the mask.  Tracked
##      alongside per-task CPU-pinning support.
##  26. Filesystem sync stubs (FSYNC, FDATASYNC, SYNC, SYNCFS) —
##      DONE returning 0.  We don't have a unified buffer-cache
##      flush mechanism yet so these are silent successes.
##      Limitation: programs that rely on these for durability
##      (databases) write at risk of crash-loss on real hardware.
##      Tracked alongside a real page-cache writeback pipeline.
##  27. SETHOSTNAME / SETDOMAINNAME — DONE as accepting stubs.
##      We don't carry a mutable hostname (uname always reports
##      "localhost").  Validates len <= 64 (Linux's
##      _UTSNAME_NODENAME_LENGTH) and the user pointer, then
##      silently discards.  setdomainname shares the
##      implementation.
##      Limitation: programs that set then read back via uname
##      see "localhost" instead of the requested name.
##  28. MLOCK / MUNLOCK / MLOCKALL / MUNLOCKALL — DONE as
##      accepting stubs.  All pages are resident on this kernel
##      (no swap), so the calls are semantically no-ops; we still
##      validate the address range so callers passing garbage see
##      EFAULT, and reject unknown MCL_* bits with EINVAL.
##      Limitation: when a swap subsystem lands, these need to
##      mark VMAs as locked so the pageout path skips them.
##  29. MSYNC — DONE as accepting stub.  Validates flag bits
##      (MS_ASYNC / MS_SYNC / MS_INVALIDATE; requires exactly one
##      of SYNC/ASYNC; rejects unknown bits), enforces 16-KiB
##      address alignment, and validates the user range.  Returns
##      0 because we don't yet have a writeback cache between
##      userspace and the page allocator.
##      Limitation: when an fs-backed page cache lands, msync must
##      actually flush dirty pages and (with MS_INVALIDATE) drop
##      cached pages so the next read picks up disk state.
##  30. FADVISE64 / READAHEAD — DONE as advisory accept.
##      fadvise64 validates POSIX_FADV_* values 0..=6, checks the
##      fd is open, and returns 0.  readahead also validates the
##      fd and returns 0.
##      Limitation: we don't act on the hints, so workloads that
##      depend on willneed-style prefetch see no speedup.
##  31. CLOSE_RANGE — DONE.  Closes (or sets CLOEXEC on) every
##      open fd in [first, last] clamped to MAX_FDS.  Honours
##      CLOSE_RANGE_CLOEXEC by toggling FD_CLOEXEC instead of
##      closing.  CLOSE_RANGE_UNSHARE is a no-op because we
##      don't share fd tables across processes (fork copies).
##      Limitation: when fd-table sharing (CLONE_FILES) lands,
##      CLOSE_RANGE_UNSHARE must allocate a private table before
##      the close loop.
##  32. GETRLIMIT / SETRLIMIT (legacy 16-byte forms) — DONE as
##      thin forwarders to sys_prlimit64 with pid=0.  Linux's
##      struct rlimit and struct rlimit64 have identical layout
##      on x86_64, so a direct shim is correct.  Inherits the
##      prlimit64 limitation: set is a silent no-op until a
##      per-process rlimit store lands.
##  33. GETCPU — DONE.  Returns the current logical CPU index
##      (via smp::current_cpu_index) and node 0.  Validates the
##      writable user pointers (each 4 bytes) and accepts NULL
##      for either output.  Limitation: we have no NUMA topology
##      so the node is hard-coded; revisit if NUMA-aware
##      scheduling lands.
##  34. STATFS / FSTATFS — DONE as synthetic stubs.  Both fill a
##      120-byte struct statfs claiming TMPFS_MAGIC, 16-KiB
##      block size, 16 GiB total / half free, 64 K inodes, 255-
##      byte name limit.  statfs validates the path pointer but
##      does not yet resolve the path; fstatfs validates the fd
##      is open in the caller's table.  Limitation: every path/fd
##      reports the same synthetic stats; when a real VFS lands
##      these should route through it and report per-mount data.
##  35. CLOCK_SETTIME / CLOCK_ADJTIME / ADJTIMEX — DONE as
##      EPERM-after-validate stubs.  We validate the user pointer
##      (16-byte timespec for clock_settime, 208-byte struct
##      timex for the others) so callers see EFAULT on garbage
##      pointers, then refuse with EPERM.  This is the sound
##      response for an unprivileged caller on Linux as well
##      (CAP_SYS_TIME required), and prevents userspace from
##      silently appearing to set a clock that the kernel
##      doesn't actually adjust.  Limitation: when a
##      time-write capability and adjustable clock land, these
##      must route through a real adjtimex/settime path.
##  36. CHROOT / MKNOD / MKNODAT — DONE as EPERM-after-validate
##      stubs.  All three require a capability no userspace
##      currently carries (CAP_SYS_CHROOT or CAP_MKNOD on
##      Linux).  We validate the path pointer (one byte) so
##      callers passing NULL or garbage see EFAULT, then refuse
##      with EPERM.  Limitation: when a per-process root state
##      and a device-node registry land, these must route
##      through real FS operations and a capability check
##      rather than a blanket refusal.
##  37. GETITIMER / SETITIMER / ALARM / PAUSE — DONE as
##      principled stubs.  Interval timers need signal-driven
##      delivery which we do not yet have.
##         - getitimer validates which (0..=2) and the output
##           pointer (32-byte itimerval), then writes zeros
##           (truthful: no timer is pending).
##         - setitimer validates which and the input pointer.
##           If the new itimerval is all-zero (a cancel) it
##           writes a zero old-value if requested and returns 0.
##           Arming a non-zero timer returns -ENOSYS so the
##           caller knows the operation cannot succeed.
##         - alarm(N) always returns 0 ("no previous alarm
##           pending"), which is truthful when N == 0 and is a
##           known lie when N > 0.  alarm() has no error return
##           in its ABI, so this is the least-bad answer; it is
##           tracked here so the eventual real implementation is
##           obvious.
##         - pause() returns -ENOSYS because the contract
##           ("block until any signal") cannot be honoured
##           without signal-driven wakeup; returning ENOSYS lets
##           userspace fall back rather than hang.
##      Limitation: when SIGALRM / SIGVTALRM / SIGPROF delivery
##      lands, these must route through it; until then, programs
##      that rely on alarm() to interrupt blocking calls will
##      not be interrupted.
##  38. ACCESS / FACCESSAT / FACCESSAT2 — DONE as
##      ENOENT-after-validate stubs.  Mode bits validated against
##      R_OK|W_OK|X_OK; bogus bits -> EINVAL.  faccessat2 also
##      validates the AT_* flag bits.  After validation, returns
##      -ENOENT because no path exists in our empty FS.
##      ENOENT is the truthful answer (the path is not present)
##      and is universally handled by loader fallback code,
##      unlike ENOSYS which can cause some loaders to bail out.
##      Limitation: when a real VFS lands these must route
##      through it and report EACCES / EOK based on real
##      permissions.
##  39. STAT / LSTAT / FSTAT / NEWFSTATAT — DONE.
##         - stat / lstat (path-based) validate the path pointer
##           and the 144-byte statbuf output pointer, then return
##           -ENOENT (no VFS, no files).
##         - fstat (fd-based) validates the statbuf pointer and
##           the fd, then synthesises a struct stat that reports
##           the correct S_IFCHR for Console, S_IFIFO for Pipe,
##           S_IFREG for File — so isatty() answers correctly on
##           our stdio fds.  Timestamps use clock_realtime().
##         - newfstatat honours AT_EMPTY_PATH by routing to fstat
##           with the dirfd, and otherwise validates the AT_*
##           flag bits and returns ENOENT for path lookups.
##      Limitation: synthetic data is per-handle-type only; when
##      a real VFS lands, stat must report real inode numbers,
##      sizes, link counts, ownership, and timestamps.
##  40. STATX — DONE following the same pattern as stat/fstat.
##      Validates the 256-byte statxbuf and the AT_* flag bits
##      (AT_EMPTY_PATH, AT_SYMLINK_NOFOLLOW, AT_NO_AUTOMOUNT,
##      AT_STATX_SYNC_AS_STAT, AT_STATX_FORCE_SYNC,
##      AT_STATX_DONT_SYNC).  AT_EMPTY_PATH routes to a
##      synthesised statx for the given fd; path lookups return
##      ENOENT.  stx_mask advertises STATX_BASIC_STATS so callers
##      know which fields are filled.  Modern glibc routes most
##      stat-family calls through statx, so this is the critical
##      one for ld.so and friends to behave.
##      Limitation: same as item 39 (no real VFS data).
##  41. MKDIR / MKDIRAT / RMDIR / UNLINK / UNLINKAT / RENAME /
##      RENAMEAT / RENAMEAT2 — DONE as pointer-validated
##      principled-errno stubs.
##         - mkdir / mkdirat validate the path pointer (NULL ->
##           EFAULT) and then return -EROFS ("read-only
##           filesystem").  EROFS is the truthful answer: the FS
##           itself is the reason create cannot succeed, and
##           installers/test runners that probe with mkdir know
##           to back off rather than retry under a different
##           path.
##         - rmdir / unlink / unlinkat validate the path
##           pointer and return -ENOENT (no files exist in our
##           empty FS).  unlinkat also validates AT_REMOVEDIR
##           (0x200) and rejects unknown flag bits with EINVAL.
##         - rename / renameat validate both old and new path
##           pointers (NULL on either -> EFAULT) and return
##           -ENOENT.  renameat2 additionally validates
##           RENAME_NOREPLACE (1) / RENAME_EXCHANGE (2) /
##           RENAME_WHITEOUT (4); any other flag bit -> EINVAL.
##      ENOENT for the destructive operations is preferred over
##      ENOSYS because POSIX-correct callers handle "no such
##      file" gracefully whereas ENOSYS often forces a hard
##      failure path.  EROFS for create lets userspace
##      distinguish "filesystem read-only" from "path missing",
##      which matters for tools that probe.
##      Limitation: when a real VFS lands, these must route
##      through it and honour real semantics; in particular,
##      mkdir under a writable mount should succeed, and
##      rename's many edge cases (EXDEV across mounts,
##      EXCHANGE atomicity, NOREPLACE conflict detection) must
##      be implemented in the VFS layer.
##  42. READLINK / READLINKAT / CHMOD family / CHOWN family /
##      TRUNCATE / FTRUNCATE / SYMLINK / SYMLINKAT / LINK /
##      LINKAT / UTIMENSAT / UTIMES / UTIME — DONE as
##      pointer-validated principled-errno stubs.
##         - readlink / readlinkat: validate path and out-buf
##           pointers, then return -EINVAL ("not a symbolic
##           link") since we have no symlinks anywhere.  This
##           is the answer ld.so and friends know how to handle
##           for paths like `/proc/self/exe` that they probe
##           opportunistically.  bufsiz == 0 -> EINVAL per Linux.
##         - chmod / fchmod / fchmodat / chown / lchown /
##           fchown / fchownat: validate path / fd, then return
##           -EROFS (read-only filesystem).  Path-NULL surfaces
##           as EFAULT; bad AT_* flag bits surface as EINVAL;
##           unknown fds surface as EBADF.  fchownat honours
##           AT_EMPTY_PATH (0x1000) by validating dirfd before
##           refusing.
##         - truncate / ftruncate: negative length -> EINVAL
##           (POSIX).  truncate(path, 0) returns EROFS; ftruncate
##           validates fd and returns EROFS for File handles,
##           EINVAL for Pipe/Console (truthful: not a regular
##           file).  ftruncate in kernel context returns EROFS
##           since there is no real FS to mutate.
##         - symlink / symlinkat / link / linkat: validate both
##           pointer operands (NULL on either -> EFAULT), reject
##           unknown linkat flag bits with EINVAL (valid =
##           AT_SYMLINK_FOLLOW | AT_EMPTY_PATH), then return
##           -EROFS.
##         - utimensat / utimes / utime: utimensat tolerates a
##           NULL path (operate on dirfd) and a NULL times
##           array (use current time); utimes/utime require a
##           non-NULL path.  Validate every non-NULL pointer
##           (16B for utimbuf, 32B for the two-timespec array
##           or two-timeval array), reject unknown utimensat
##           flag bits with EINVAL (only AT_SYMLINK_NOFOLLOW
##           is valid), then return -EROFS.
##      EROFS is preferred over ENOSYS for the create / mutate
##      operations because POSIX-correct callers handle EROFS as
##      "FS is read-only; back off" while ENOSYS can force a
##      hard-failure path.  EINVAL for readlink is what every
##      modern loader treats as "this path is not a symlink";
##      lying with ENOENT would suggest the path is just missing
##      and might invite retries.
##      Limitation: when a real VFS lands, these must route
##      through it.  In particular truncate, ftruncate(File),
##      and all chmod/chown variants must honour real
##      permissions and EROFS only when the underlying mount is
##      read-only; readlink/readlinkat must read real symlink
##      targets where they exist; the utime family must persist
##      timestamps in inode metadata.  When a CAP_FOWNER /
##      CAP_CHOWN check is added, chown/fchown/lchown/fchownat
##      should also return EPERM when the calling process lacks
##      the capability and the operation would otherwise have
##      succeeded.
##  43. SIGNALFD / SIGNALFD4 / TIMERFD_CREATE / TIMERFD_SETTIME /
##      TIMERFD_GETTIME / INOTIFY_INIT / INOTIFY_INIT1 /
##      INOTIFY_ADD_WATCH / INOTIFY_RM_WATCH / FANOTIFY_INIT /
##      FANOTIFY_MARK — DONE as input-validated ENOSYS stubs.
##         - signalfd / signalfd4: sigsetsize != 8 -> EINVAL,
##           NULL mask -> EFAULT, bogus flags -> EINVAL, then
##           -ENOSYS.
##         - timerfd_create: clockid must be one of
##           CLOCK_REALTIME (0) / CLOCK_MONOTONIC (1) /
##           CLOCK_BOOTTIME (7) / CLOCK_REALTIME_ALARM (8) /
##           CLOCK_BOOTTIME_ALARM (9) — anything else EINVAL;
##           flags validate against TFD_NONBLOCK | TFD_CLOEXEC;
##           then -ENOSYS.
##         - timerfd_settime: flags validate against
##           TFD_TIMER_ABSTIME | TFD_TIMER_CANCEL_ON_SET, new
##           value pointer validated (32B itimerspec), old
##           pointer validated for write if non-NULL.  Then fd
##           is looked up; in kernel context or for a non-
##           timerfd fd this collapses to EBADF / EINVAL
##           rather than ENOSYS because the input shape was
##           valid but no timerfd exists in our world.
##         - timerfd_gettime: same shape; curr ptr validated
##           for write (32B), then EBADF/EINVAL.
##         - inotify_init / inotify_init1: -ENOSYS.  init1
##           validates IN_NONBLOCK | IN_CLOEXEC.
##         - inotify_add_watch: NULL path -> EFAULT,
##           mask == 0 -> EINVAL, then EBADF (no inotify fd
##           exists).
##         - inotify_rm_watch: EBADF.
##         - fanotify_init / fanotify_mark: -ENOSYS;
##           fanotify_mark validates a non-NULL path pointer
##           before refusing so EFAULT can still surface.
##      ENOSYS is the right answer for these because each one
##      *creates* an fd that nothing else in the kernel knows
##      how to read or wait on — pretending success would leave
##      userspace with an unusable fd.  glibc, systemd-notify,
##      and event-loop libraries all treat -ENOSYS as "this
##      kernel doesn't have signalfd / timerfd / inotify" and
##      fall back to alarm + signals / threads + nanosleep /
##      polling-based file watch respectively, which gives the
##      best-available behaviour with no further work.
##      Limitation: when a real timer wheel and a file-change
##      notification subsystem land, these must be wired
##      through them.  Inotify in particular needs FS metadata
##      change events bubbled up from the VFS layer, so it is
##      blocked on real VFS more than on its own kernel object.
##  44. SENDFILE / SPLICE / TEE / VMSPLICE / COPY_FILE_RANGE /
##      AIO (io_setup family) / IO_URING family — DONE as
##      input-validated principled-errno stubs.
##         - sendfile / splice / tee / vmsplice / copy_file_range
##           validate flag bits (splice/tee/vmsplice:
##           SPLICE_F_MOVE | NONBLOCK | MORE | GIFT;
##           copy_file_range: must be 0), fds (via
##           linux_fd_lookup outside kernel context), and
##           offset / iov pointers, then return -EINVAL.
##           EINVAL is the right choice here because POSIX
##           callers and glibc already handle "this fd shape
##           isn't compatible with the zero-copy syscall" by
##           falling back to a read/write loop; ENOSYS would
##           suggest the call doesn't exist at all and could
##           pick a worse code path.
##         - io_setup / io_destroy / io_submit / io_cancel /
##           io_getevents (POSIX AIO): io_setup validates
##           nr_events != 0, validates the ctx_idp output
##           pointer (8B aio_context_t), then -ENOSYS so glibc
##           falls back to thread-pool AIO.  The other AIO
##           syscalls return -EINVAL because no context handle
##           is ever valid.
##         - io_uring_setup / io_uring_enter / io_uring_register:
##           io_uring_setup validates entries != 0 and the
##           120-byte struct io_uring_params output pointer,
##           then -ENOSYS so io_uring-aware callers fall back
##           to epoll.  enter / register are unconditional
##           -ENOSYS.
##      Limitation: real implementations need page-cache
##      page transfer for sendfile, pipe-internal page move
##      for splice/tee, gather-write for vmsplice, an iouring
##      submission queue / completion queue, and an AIO
##      thread-pool or async runtime.  All of these are
##      blocked on the kernel growing real async-I/O
##      infrastructure (already partly in place via the
##      kernel-side io_uring shim, but not Linux-shaped).
##  45. BPF / PERF_EVENT_OPEN / KEYCTL / ADD_KEY / REQUEST_KEY /
##      USERFAULTFD / MEMFD_CREATE / MEMFD_SECRET / PIDFD_OPEN /
##      PIDFD_SEND_SIGNAL / PIDFD_GETFD / PROCESS_VM_READV /
##      PROCESS_VM_WRITEV / PROCESS_MRELEASE — DONE as
##      input-validated principled-errno stubs.
##         - bpf: validates size != 0, attr pointer non-NULL
##           and readable for `size` bytes, then -ENOSYS.
##         - perf_event_open: validates attr pointer (at least
##           the 8-byte size header), then -ENOSYS.
##         - keyctl / add_key / request_key: keyctl is
##           unconditional ENOSYS; add_key / request_key
##           require non-NULL type & description pointers
##           before refusing.
##         - userfaultfd: validates UFFD_USER_MODE_ONLY |
##           O_CLOEXEC | O_NONBLOCK; bogus -> EINVAL; then
##           -ENOSYS so callers fall back to a SIGSEGV
##           handler if they really need page-fault notify.
##         - memfd_create / memfd_secret: validate name and
##           flags (memfd_create: MFD_CLOEXEC | ALLOW_SEALING |
##           HUGETLB | NOEXEC_SEAL | EXEC plus huge-page-size
##           bits 26..31; memfd_secret: O_CLOEXEC).  Then
##           -ENOSYS so mesa/Vulkan/Wayland fall back to
##           shm_open()-via-tmpfs.
##         - pidfd_open: pid <= 0 -> EINVAL, validates
##           PIDFD_NONBLOCK, then -ENOSYS so callers fall back
##           to /proc/PID path lookup.
##         - pidfd_send_signal: flags must be 0, sig in
##           [0,64], siginfo pointer (128B) if non-NULL,
##           fd via linux_fd_lookup, then -EINVAL (pidfd is
##           not actually a pidfd in our world).
##         - pidfd_getfd: flags reserved (must be 0), fd
##           validated, then -EINVAL.
##         - process_vm_readv / process_vm_writev: flags must
##           be 0, iovcnt clamped to 1024 (IOV_MAX), iovec
##           pointers validated when nonzero count, then
##           -ESRCH (no target process can be addressed).
##         - process_mrelease: flags must be 0; then -ENOSYS.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * ENOSYS is right for the FD-creating syscalls
##           (BPF, perf_event_open, keyctl, userfaultfd,
##           memfd*, pidfd_open) because feature-detection
##           code looks for it and falls back; pretending
##           success would hand back an unusable fd.
##         * EINVAL is right for pidfd_send_signal /
##           pidfd_getfd because the fd is real but not a
##           pidfd in our kernel.
##         * ESRCH is right for process_vm_* because the
##           target process does not exist from our point of
##           view; this is also what Linux returns for a
##           missing pid.
##      Limitation: when real BPF / perf / keyring / memfd /
##      pidfd / process-cross-VM facilities land, these
##      stubs must be replaced.  Of these, memfd_create is
##      the highest-priority for desktop apps (Vulkan, Wayland,
##      sandboxes); the rest are mostly used by tracing /
##      privileged tools that handle missing-feature paths
##      gracefully.
##  46. XATTR family (set / get / list / remove × path / l /
##      f variants = 12 syscalls), QUOTACTL / QUOTACTL_FD,
##      INIT_MODULE / FINIT_MODULE / DELETE_MODULE, UNSHARE /
##      SETNS, MOUNT / UMOUNT2 / PIVOT_ROOT, SWAPON / SWAPOFF,
##      REBOOT, SYSLOG — DONE as input-validated principled-
##      errno stubs.
##         - Extended attributes:
##              * set / remove (12 variants) -> EOPNOTSUPP
##                ("filesystem does not support xattrs") so
##                callers that test feature support fall back
##                gracefully.
##              * get -> ENODATA ("attribute does not exist")
##                so callers see the right errno for a missing
##                attribute, which they all handle.
##              * list -> 0 (empty list) since no attributes
##                exist; this is the truthful answer and lets
##                portable code complete without error.
##         - quotactl / quotactl_fd: EPERM after validating
##           any non-NULL special pointer / fd.  Quotas are a
##           privileged feature and the truthful answer is
##           "you lack CAP_SYS_ADMIN".
##         - init_module / finit_module / delete_module:
##           validate the module image / fd / name pointers
##           and the flag bits (MODULE_INIT_IGNORE_MODVERSIONS |
##           IGNORE_VERMAGIC | COMPRESSED_FILE for finit;
##           O_NONBLOCK | O_TRUNC for delete), then EPERM.
##         - unshare: validate the CLONE_* flag mask;
##           unshare(0) succeeds (trivial); anything else
##           EPERM until namespace plumbing exists.
##         - setns: validate fd; EPERM.
##         - mount: validate target (required), source / type /
##           data (optional); EPERM.  umount2 validates MNT_FORCE
##           | DETACH | EXPIRE | UMOUNT_NOFOLLOW; pivot_root
##           validates both pointers; all EPERM.
##         - swapon / swapoff: validate path; EPERM.
##         - reboot: requires LINUX_REBOOT_MAGIC1 (0xfee1dead);
##           bad magic -> EINVAL; valid magic -> EPERM.
##         - syslog: type 0..=10 valid, anything else EINVAL.
##           SIZE_BUFFER (6 / 9) and SIZE_UNREAD (7 / 10)
##           return 0 (truthful: no log).  READ family (2 / 3 /
##           4) validates buf/len then EPERM.  Other types
##           return EPERM.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * EOPNOTSUPP / ENODATA for xattr is the universal
##           portable-code answer and avoids "ENOSYS makes
##           glibc behave weirdly" failures observed with some
##           hardened userspace.
##         * EPERM for privileged operations matches what a
##           non-root Linux process sees, which is also the
##           expected behaviour of a microkernel that simply
##           doesn't give userspace these capabilities.
##         * unshare(0) -> 0 is exactly what Linux does and is
##           a common idiom in init systems to detect support.
##      Limitation: when a real VFS lands and xattr storage is
##      added, set/get/list/remove must route through it.
##      When (and if) a kernel-module loader is added,
##      init_module/finit_module/delete_module need to do real
##      work.  Namespaces and mount need actual namespace and
##      mount-tree infrastructure.  reboot needs ACPI shutdown
##      / restart wiring.  syslog needs hookup to the kernel's
##      log buffer (which already exists for our serial
##      logger; just not Linux-shaped klogd buffer).
##  47. SysV IPC (SHMGET / SHMAT / SHMCTL / SHMDT, SEMGET /
##      SEMOP / SEMCTL / SEMTIMEDOP, MSGGET / MSGSND / MSGRCV /
##      MSGCTL) + POSIX message queues (MQ_OPEN / MQ_UNLINK /
##      MQ_TIMEDSEND / MQ_TIMEDRECEIVE / MQ_NOTIFY /
##      MQ_GETSETATTR) — 18 syscalls, DONE as input-validated
##      principled-errno stubs.
##         - Lookup syscalls (shmget / semget / msgget /
##           mq_open) -> ENOSYS so feature-detection code in
##           glibc / portable userspace falls back to the
##           POSIX-shm / pipe / futex equivalents which we
##           already implement.
##         - "Operate on an existing IPC id" syscalls
##           (shmat / shmctl / shmdt / semop / semtimedop /
##           semctl / msgsnd / msgrcv / msgctl) validate the
##           user buffers (sembuf is 6 bytes, sigevent / mq_attr
##           are 64 bytes, two timespecs are 32 bytes, etc.)
##           then return EINVAL.  EINVAL is the Linux answer
##           for a stale / unknown IPC id and is what callers
##           that handle "the segment was destroyed" expect.
##         - mq_unlink validates the name then returns ENOENT
##           (no such mq).  mq_timedsend / mq_timedreceive /
##           mq_notify / mq_getsetattr validate the
##           buffers + timespecs + fd kind then return EBADF
##           because the mqd_t cannot be a real mq descriptor
##           in our kernel; EBADF is what glibc maps to "your
##           mq is gone" which all callers handle.
##         - semop / semtimedop reject nsops == 0 with EINVAL
##           and nsops > IOV_MAX (1024) with E2BIG-style EINVAL,
##           matching Linux validation order.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * ENOSYS for the four lookup syscalls is the only
##           answer that actually fires the userspace fallback.
##           Pretending success would hand back a key that no
##           subsequent shmat / msgsnd / semop / mq_timedsend
##           call could honour, and every cold path through
##           those would then trip an assertion in libc.
##         * EINVAL for the stale-id operations is the answer
##           Linux gives for a destroyed segment / set / queue,
##           which all SysV-IPC-using code handles because
##           segments are routinely destroyed under the caller.
##         * EBADF for the mq fd-operations mirrors POSIX's
##           "mqd_t is a file descriptor in Linux" model and
##           is what mq_close / mq_send map to when the
##           descriptor is closed elsewhere.
##      Limitation: when (and if) SysV IPC and POSIX message
##      queues are wired up, replace these with real
##      implementations.  Most modern userspace prefers POSIX
##      shm + futex + pipes / sockets and never touches these
##      syscalls; the main historical exception is X11, which
##      is not on our roadmap (we're going Wayland-only).
##      Notable users that DO exercise these in the wild:
##      Oracle DB and PostgreSQL (SysV shm fallback when POSIX
##      shm is unavailable — but both prefer POSIX shm when
##      offered), and a handful of embedded message-passing
##      daemons that use POSIX mq.
##  48. POLL / PPOLL / SELECT / PSELECT6 + epoll family
##      (EPOLL_CREATE / EPOLL_CREATE1 / EPOLL_CTL / EPOLL_WAIT /
##      EPOLL_PWAIT / EPOLL_PWAIT2) — 10 syscalls, DONE as
##      input-validated principled-errno stubs that all return
##      ENOSYS / EBADF / EINVAL.
##         - poll / ppoll / select / pselect6 / epoll_create /
##           epoll_create1: validate every user pointer
##           (pollfd is 8 bytes; fd_set is ceil(nfds/8) bytes;
##           timespec is 16; timeval is 16; sigset_t is 8;
##           pselect6's last arg is a 16-byte {ss*, size_t}
##           struct; epoll_event is 12) and every flag bit,
##           then return ENOSYS.  Why ENOSYS rather than
##           silently returning 0 (timeout) — because programs
##           that depend on poll/epoll for their event loop
##           (every server, every libuv / tokio program) would
##           otherwise busy-loop forever waiting for events
##           that never fire.  ENOSYS is the only error code
##           that propagates back to the caller in a way they
##           can observe.  Programs that want graceful
##           feature-fallback (rare for modern code; common
##           historically with select -> poll -> epoll) see the
##           expected error from the most-advanced syscall.
##         - epoll_ctl: validates op (ADD | DEL | MOD), the
##           12-byte epoll_event ptr for ADD / MOD, and the
##           target fd, then returns EBADF on the epfd.  EBADF
##           is the right answer because epoll_create returned
##           ENOSYS so no caller can hold a real epfd; this is
##           also what Linux returns for a closed-out epfd.
##         - epoll_wait / epoll_pwait / epoll_pwait2: validate
##           the events ptr (maxevents * 12 bytes), maxevents
##           > 0 (EINVAL otherwise), the optional timespec and
##           sigmask, then EBADF for the same reason.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * Silent return-0 would hang every event loop.  An
##           explicit ENOSYS is the only answer modern userspace
##           handles in a recoverable way (it propagates as
##           ENOSYS up to the I/O multiplexer's init code,
##           which fails fast and prints a useful message).
##         * EBADF on epoll_ctl / wait matches what Linux
##           returns after the epfd was closed by another
##           thread, which is a real wire-shape every caller
##           already handles.
##      Limitation: when readiness multiplexing lands on top
##      of console / pipe / file / socket fds, these stubs are
##      replaced by dispatches into the readiness subsystem.
##      Real epoll requires per-fd readiness state, an
##      interest-set / ready-set queue per epoll-fd, and
##      level- vs edge-triggered semantics.  Estimated effort:
##      ~3-4 weeks for a feature-complete implementation
##      including poll / ppoll / select / pselect6 translation
##      to the same readiness primitives.  Until then, server
##      programs (HTTP, SSH, X.org / Wayland compositors,
##      databases, async runtimes) cannot run; only synchronous
##      blocking-I/O programs (shells, coreutils, batch jobs)
##      will work.
##  49. OPENAT2 / EXECVEAT / NAME_TO_HANDLE_AT /
##      OPEN_BY_HANDLE_AT + new mount API (FSOPEN / FSCONFIG /
##      FSMOUNT / FSPICK / OPEN_TREE / MOVE_MOUNT) — 10
##      syscalls DONE as input-validated principled-errno
##      stubs.
##         - openat2: validate path + struct open_how (24
##           bytes: u64 flags, u64 mode, u64 resolve) + size
##           == 24, then ENOSYS so glibc / io_uring fall back
##           to openat (which we implement).
##         - execveat: validate AT_EMPTY_PATH | AT_SYMLINK_NOFOLLOW
##           flags + path (or empty path when AT_EMPTY_PATH) +
##           argv / envp head pointers, then ENOSYS so callers
##           fall back to execve (which we implement).
##         - name_to_handle_at: validate AT_EMPTY_PATH |
##           AT_SYMLINK_FOLLOW | AT_HANDLE_FID flags, path,
##           mount_id ptr (4B), handle header (8B), then
##           EOPNOTSUPP — the canonical answer for "this
##           filesystem does not export persistent handles",
##           which every caller handles (tmpfs returns this).
##         - open_by_handle_at: validate handle header (8B),
##           then EPERM (this syscall requires
##           CAP_DAC_READ_SEARCH on Linux).
##         - fsopen / fsmount / fspick / fsconfig: validate
##           the FSOPEN_CLOEXEC / FSMOUNT_CLOEXEC / FSPICK_*
##           and MOUNT_ATTR_* / FSCONFIG cmd ranges + every
##           pointer, then EPERM (privileged mount API).
##         - open_tree: validate OPEN_TREE_CLONE | O_CLOEXEC |
##           AT_EMPTY_PATH | AT_SYMLINK_NOFOLLOW | AT_NO_AUTOMOUNT
##           | AT_RECURSIVE + path (or empty path), EPERM.
##         - move_mount: validate the 8-bit MOVE_MOUNT_* flag
##           mask + both paths (each optional with EMPTY_PATH),
##           EPERM.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * ENOSYS for openat2 / execveat is what glibc /
##           io_uring expect from a pre-5.6 kernel and they
##           fall back gracefully.  Pretending success without
##           implementing the resolve restrictions of openat2
##           would be a security bug — the whole point of
##           openat2 is to enforce RESOLVE_NO_SYMLINKS /
##           NO_MAGICLINKS / IN_ROOT etc.
##         * EOPNOTSUPP for name_to_handle_at is the right
##           answer for filesystems without persistent ids
##           (tmpfs, fuse without export_operations, etc).
##         * EPERM for the new mount API mirrors what
##           non-CAP_SYS_ADMIN Linux processes see and is what
##           every container runtime / mount helper handles
##           on a hardened host.
##      Limitation: when the VFS lands and we add mount-tree
##      support, fsopen / fsconfig / fsmount / fspick /
##      open_tree / move_mount become the new mount UI for
##      portable code.  openat2's resolve flags must be
##      implemented in the path-walk code at the same time —
##      if we add openat2 before then, we MUST implement
##      RESOLVE_BENEATH / IN_ROOT / NO_SYMLINKS or it becomes
##      a path-traversal escape valve.
##  50. NUMA memory-policy family (MBIND / SET_MEMPOLICY /
##      GET_MEMPOLICY / MIGRATE_PAGES / MOVE_PAGES) +
##      SCHED_SETATTR / SCHED_GETATTR + Landlock
##      (LANDLOCK_CREATE_RULESET / ADD_RULE / RESTRICT_SELF) +
##      KCMP + RESTART_SYSCALL — 12 syscalls DONE as input-
##      validated principled-errno stubs.
##         - NUMA: validate the MPOL_DEFAULT / PREFERRED / BIND /
##           INTERLEAVE / LOCAL / PREFERRED_MANY mode + MPOL_F_*
##           mode flags + nodemask pointers (ceil(maxnode/8)
##           bytes, capped at 1 MiB worth of bits) + MPOL_MF_MOVE
##           / MOVE_ALL / STRICT flags + count caps; then ENOSYS
##           so libnuma-style callers know we are single-node
##           UMA.
##         - sched_setattr: validate non-zero flags (EINVAL) and
##           sched_attr ptr; then EPERM (SCHED_DEADLINE requires
##           CAP_SYS_NICE; we cannot honour it).
##         - sched_getattr: validate size in [48, 1 MiB] and
##           writable buffer; then ENOSYS so glibc's
##           sched_getscheduler / sched_getparam fallback fires.
##         - Landlock:
##              * landlock_create_ruleset with
##                LANDLOCK_CREATE_RULESET_VERSION returns 0
##                (= "ABI v0 = no Landlock") — the honest
##                answer; portable code uses this exact value
##                to detect absence and skip sandboxing.
##              * Real ruleset-creation path validates the
##                attr ptr + 8..=1MiB size, then ENOSYS.
##              * landlock_add_rule validates rule_type
##                (1 = PATH_BENEATH | 2 = NET_PORT) + 16-byte
##                rule_attr, then EBADF (the ruleset fd cannot
##                exist).
##              * landlock_restrict_self: flags must be 0,
##                then EBADF for the same reason.
##         - kcmp: validate type ∈ 0..=7 + non-negative pids;
##           ESRCH for negative pid (matches Linux), else ENOSYS.
##         - restart_syscall: -EINTR (no saved syscall to
##           restart; matches Linux behaviour for a stale
##           restart frame).
##      Choice rationale:
##         * The Landlock version-query returning 0 is critical.
##           If we returned ENOSYS, portable sandbox code (Tor,
##           systemd, sandbox-helpers in browsers) would log a
##           noisy "unexpected error querying Landlock version"
##           rather than silently skipping it.  Returning 0
##           tells them "version 0 = no Landlock = skip".
##         * ENOSYS for the NUMA syscalls is correct because
##           libnuma probes /sys/devices/system/node/possible
##           first; on a single-node system the syscalls are
##           never called.  The few callers that hit them
##           anyway handle ENOSYS gracefully.
##         * EPERM for sched_setattr avoids granting privileged
##           SCHED_DEADLINE without enforcing the bandwidth /
##           admission-control guarantees DEADLINE requires —
##           a partial implementation would be a real-time
##           correctness bug.
##         * EINTR for restart_syscall matches what the Linux
##           kernel does when a userspace process makes a
##           direct (incorrect) call.  ENOSYS would be wrong
##           because the syscall number IS valid; the syscall
##           itself just has no state to restart from.
##      Limitation: NUMA hardware support is gated on a real
##      SRAT-parsing path through ACPI + per-node page lists
##      + per-task mempolicy + page-migration; estimated ~2-3
##      months of work and not on the desktop-OS critical path.
##      sched_setattr / DEADLINE require an EDF / global-EDF
##      scheduler with proper admission control — out of scope
##      until real-time workloads are a requirement.  Landlock
##      requires path-based access control hooks throughout the
##      VFS; it is a strong defense-in-depth feature for desktop
##      sandboxing but depends on the VFS landing first.
##  51. SECCOMP / PTRACE / CLONE3 / MEMBARRIER / RSEQ /
##      SYNC_FILE_RANGE / PROCESS_MADVISE / CACHESTAT / MSEAL /
##      MAP_SHADOW_STACK — 10 syscalls DONE as input-validated
##      principled-errno stubs.
##         - seccomp: validate op ∈ 0..=3 (SET_MODE_STRICT,
##           SET_MODE_FILTER, GET_ACTION_AVAIL, GET_NOTIF_SIZES)
##           and flag/args requirements per op, then ENOSYS so
##           programs run without a BPF filter.
##         - ptrace: cap req at 0x10_000, ESRCH for negative
##           pid, otherwise EPERM (the answer for an
##           untraceable target on Linux).  gdb / strace / perf
##           handle this gracefully.
##         - clone3: validate args ptr + size ∈ [88, 1 MiB]
##           (struct clone_args is 88 bytes minimum), then
##           ENOSYS so glibc falls back to clone (implemented).
##         - membarrier: cmd 0 (QUERY) returns 0 (no commands
##           supported); other cmds get EINVAL.  libstdc++
##           asymmetric-barriers / Folly handle this.
##         - rseq: validate len == 32 + flags ∈ {0, 1} +
##           non-NULL ptr, then ENOSYS so glibc skips
##           registration.
##         - sync_file_range: validate WAIT_BEFORE | WRITE |
##           WAIT_AFTER flag mask + non-negative off/nbytes +
##           fd, then 0 (truthful: all our filesystems write
##           through; no buffered cache to flush yet).
##         - process_madvise: validate flags == 0 + iov_cnt ≤
##           IOV_MAX + 16B iovec entries + advice ≤ 100 + fd,
##           then EBADF (no real pidfd).
##         - cachestat: validate flags == 0 + 16B range ptr +
##           32B stats writable ptr + fd, then ENOSYS.
##         - mseal: validate flags == 0 + addr + len no
##           overflow, then ENOSYS.  Memory-sealing is a
##           hardening feature; absence is fine.
##         - map_shadow_stack: validate size % 8 == 0 + non-
##           zero + SHADOW_STACK_SET_TOKEN flag bit, then
##           ENOSYS (CET shadow stacks require hardware +
##           kernel infrastructure not yet wired).
##      Choice rationale:
##         * sync_file_range returns 0 because the operation
##           is semantically a no-op — we have no buffered
##           write cache to flush.  Userspace callers (mostly
##           databases like PostgreSQL using SYNC_FILE_RANGE
##           to bound fsync latency) get correct behaviour.
##         * membarrier QUERY returning 0 (no commands)
##           matches what Linux returns for an unsupported
##           build; portable code skips memory barriers and
##           falls back to seq_cst, which the ISA gives us
##           naturally.
##         * ENOSYS for seccomp lets unprivileged code run
##           without a filter.  This is a real loss of
##           defense-in-depth — when (and if) we add seccomp
##           filtering, it should be an EBPF-style filter in
##           the syscall dispatcher, NOT pretended-success
##           which would be a security-misadvertisement bug.
##      Limitation: when ptrace, seccomp, clone3, rseq,
##      membarrier, or shadow-stack land for real, these stubs
##      get replaced.  ptrace is by far the highest-priority
##      for desktop usability (gdb, strace, perf, debuggers
##      need it).  clone3 is the second-highest because every
##      modern Linux libc uses it as the primary thread-spawn
##      path.  seccomp is third (sandboxes).  The rest are
##      lower-priority since their absence is well-handled.
##  52. RT_SIGSUSPEND / RT_SIGTIMEDWAIT / RT_SIGQUEUEINFO /
##      RT_TGSIGQUEUEINFO + POSIX timer family (TIMER_CREATE /
##      _DELETE / _SETTIME / _GETTIME / _GETOVERRUN) — 9
##      syscalls DONE as input-validated principled-errno
##      stubs.
##         - rt_sigsuspend: validate sigsetsize == 8 +
##           non-NULL mask; return EINTR (documented wake-up
##           answer when a handler ran during suspend; every
##           caller handles it because it's the ONLY way
##           sigsuspend ever returns).
##         - rt_sigtimedwait: validate sigsetsize == 8 + mask
##           + optional 128B siginfo writable + optional 16B
##           timespec; return EAGAIN (documented "timeout
##           expired without matching signal" answer).  NULL
##           timeout (= wait forever) ALSO returns EAGAIN to
##           avoid hanging; this is mildly hostile but the
##           alternative is unbounded block.
##         - rt_sigqueueinfo: validate sig ∈ 0..=64 + 128B
##           siginfo ptr; forward to existing kill() semantics
##           (siginfo payload is dropped because our dispatch
##           does not carry it).
##         - rt_tgsigqueueinfo: same but forward to tgkill().
##         - timer_create: validate clockid ∈ 0..=11 (REALTIME
##           through TAI) + optional 64B sigevent + required
##           4B timerid_t writable; return ENOSYS.
##         - timer_delete / timer_getoverrun: EINVAL (no
##           timers exist — any timerid is unknown).
##         - timer_settime: validate TIMER_ABSTIME flag + 32B
##           itimerspec read + optional 32B old_value write;
##           EINVAL.
##         - timer_gettime: validate 32B curr_value write;
##           EINVAL.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * sigsuspend returning EINTR rather than blocking
##           forever is essential — userspace event-loop
##           helpers use sigsuspend during signal-safe shutdown
##           and would hang the entire process otherwise.
##         * sigtimedwait with NULL timeout returning EAGAIN is
##           the only safe choice without real signal delivery.
##           Programs that use SIGCHLD reaping (test runners,
##           init systems) will see EAGAIN and fall back to
##           polling waitpid, which is implemented.
##         * Forwarding rt_sigqueueinfo to kill is correct
##           except for the siginfo payload, which is rarely
##           consumed (most callers fire-and-forget the signal).
##         * EINVAL for stale timerid_t matches Linux when a
##           timer was destroyed by a different thread.
##      Limitation: when real signal delivery + per-process
##      POSIX timers land, these stubs are replaced.  Per-
##      process timers are needed for clock(2) /
##      pthread_cond_timedwait fallback paths but most modern
##      code uses timerfd_create or epoll_pwait2 instead;
##      these are also stubs above so the transitive impact is
##      limited.  RT_SIGRETURN is the signal-trampoline
##      return path and has a frame-level implementation
##      elsewhere; it is NOT dispatched through
##      dispatch_linux().
##  53. BSD-socket family (SOCKET / SOCKETPAIR / BIND / LISTEN /
##      ACCEPT / ACCEPT4 / CONNECT / GETSOCKNAME / GETPEERNAME /
##      SENDTO / RECVFROM / SENDMSG / RECVMSG / SENDMMSG /
##      RECVMMSG / SETSOCKOPT / GETSOCKOPT / SHUTDOWN) — 18
##      syscalls DONE as input-validated principled-errno stubs.
##         - socket: validate domain ∈ {AF_UNIX, AF_INET,
##           AF_INET6, AF_NETLINK, AF_PACKET} + type low 4 bits
##           ∈ 1..=5 + only SOCK_CLOEXEC|SOCK_NONBLOCK flag bits;
##           return ENOSYS.  This is the canonical "no networking
##           in this kernel" answer that userspace probes (musl
##           getaddrinfo, OpenSSL self-tests, etc.) handle
##           gracefully.
##         - socketpair: validate domain == AF_UNIX + same type
##           rules + 8B sv[2] writable; return ENOSYS.
##         - bind / listen / accept / accept4 / connect /
##           getsockname / getpeername / sendto / recvfrom /
##           sendmsg / recvmsg / sendmmsg / recvmmsg / setsockopt
##           / getsockopt / shutdown: validate sockaddr lens (>=
##           2B for sa_family read; addrlen* 4B read+write), iov
##           pointers, msghdr (56B), mmsghdr (64B per entry),
##           flag bits where defined; then return EBADF.  This
##           matches what real Linux would say if userspace
##           passed a non-socket fd, because in our kernel no
##           socket fd can possibly exist (socket() returns
##           ENOSYS).  Selecting EBADF over EOPNOTSUPP keeps the
##           "any fd you pass is wrong" worldview consistent and
##           lets callers fall back to non-socket I/O.
##      Choice rationale:
##         * ENOSYS for socket/socketpair is exactly the signal
##           the C library's getaddrinfo / resolver path uses to
##           switch to local-only resolution.  EAFNOSUPPORT (97)
##           would also be defensible but requires a new errno
##           constant and most lookup code only special-cases
##           ENOSYS.
##         * EBADF for the operate-on-existing-socket calls is
##           the correct answer for "you passed an fd to an open
##           file but it isn't a socket" — userspace SSL/HTTP
##           libraries check for EBADF before reading errors.
##         * shutdown validates how ∈ {SHUT_RD=0, SHUT_WR=1,
##           SHUT_RDWR=2} so callers that probe with bogus
##           values still get a useful answer.
##         * setsockopt/getsockopt level == -1 (i.e. socklen_t
##           interpreted as i32) is EINVAL because real Linux
##           rejects negative level values; we use this to gate
##           the validation cheaply.
##      Limitation: when the network stack lands these stubs are
##      replaced by direct dispatch into the AF_INET / AF_INET6 /
##      AF_UNIX subsystems.  The errno choices preserve the
##      current "no socket exists" worldview, so every existing
##      call site continues to work — adding real sockets is a
##      pure addition.  Highest-priority follow-up is AF_UNIX
##      socketpair() for libc helper threads (pthread cancellation
##      pipes) and gRPC unix sockets.  AF_INET/INET6 come later
##      with the TCP/IP stack.  Also: setsockopt/getsockopt only
##      validate buffer reachability — not (level, optname)
##      combinations — because the latter requires a real socket
